2:26:1577:0:14:72:294:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Credit Frictions and Optimal Monetary Policy
2:27:1621:14:14:72:253:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Vasco Cúrdia and Michael Woodford
2:28:1654:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 21820
2:29:1682:14:14:72:148:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:December 2015
2:30:1695:14:28:72:157:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. E44,E52
2:31:1710:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:32:1718:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:We extend the basic (representative-household) New Keynesian [NK] model of the monetary transmission
2:33:1818:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:mechanism to allow for a spread between the interest rate available to savers and borrowers, that can
2:34:1919:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:vary for either exogenous or endogenous reasons. We find that the mere existence of a positive average
2:35:2021:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:spread makes little quantitative difference for the predicted effects of particular policies. Variation
2:36:2124:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:in spreads over time is of greater significance, with consequences both for the equilibrium relation
2:37:2224:14:28:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:between the policy rate and aggregate expenditure and for the relation between real activity and inflation.
2:38:2331:28:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:Nonetheless, we find that the target criterion—a linear relation that should be maintained between
2:39:2429:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:the inflation rate and changes in the output gap—that characterizes optimal policy in the basic NK
2:40:2527:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:model continues to provide a good approximation to optimal policy, even in the presence of variations
2:41:2628:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:in credit spreads. Such a "flexible inflation target" can be implemented by a central-bank reaction
2:42:2727:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:F:function that is similar to a forward-looking Taylor rule, but adjusted for changes in current and expected
2:43:2834:14:42:72:173:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:future credit spreads.
2:44:2856:42:14:72:138:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Vasco Cúrdia
2:45:2868:14:14:72:262:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:Federal Reserve Bank of San Francisco
2:46:2905:14:14:72:209:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:101 Market Street, MS 1130
2:47:2931:14:14:72:195:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:San Francisco, CA 94105
2:48:2954:14:28:72:188:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:vasco.curdia@sf.frb.org
2:49:2977:28:14:72:164:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:Michael Woodford
2:50:2993:14:14:72:198:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:51:3016:14:14:72:173:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Columbia University
2:52:3035:14:14:72:169:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:420 W. 118th Street
2:53:3054:14:14:72:179:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:New York, NY 10027
2:54:3072:14:14:72:124:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:55:3080:14:0:72:190:210:12:Times:12:Times:C:mw2230@columbia.edu
3:56:3143:0:30:72:208:687:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:57:3160:30:18:72:540:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:It is common for theoretical evaluations of alternative monetary policies — most notably,
3:58:3249:18:18:72:540:639:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the literature that provides theoretical foundations for inflation targeting — to be conducted
3:59:3343:18:18:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using models of the monetary transmission mechanism that abstract altogether from financial
3:60:3434:18:18:72:539:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frictions.1There is generally assumed to be a single interest rate — “theinterest rate” —
3:61:3523:18:18:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that is at once the policy rate that constitutes the operating target for the central bank, the
3:62:3618:18:18:72:540:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate of return that all households and firms receive on savings, and the rate at which anyone
3:63:3711:18:18:72:540:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can borrow against future income.  In models with more complete theoretical foundations,
3:64:3799:18:18:72:540:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this  is  justified  by  assuming  frictionless  financial  markets,  in  which  all  interest  rates  (of
3:65:3905:18:18:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similar maturity) must be equal in order for arbitrage opportunities not to exist.  It is also
3:66:3999:18:17:72:540:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:common to assume a representative household, and firms that maximize the value of their
3:67:4086:17:18:72:540:478:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings streams to that household, so that there is no need for credit flows in equilibrium in
3:68:4181:18:18:72:540:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:any event; such models imply that a breakdown of credit markets would have no allocative
3:69:4269:18:18:72:540:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significance.  Many of the quantitative DSGE models developed in central banks and other
3:70:4357:18:18:72:442:424:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:policy institutions before the recent financial crisis share these features.2
3:71:4434:18:18:89:539:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Such models abstract from important complications of actual economies, even those that
3:72:4520:18:18:71:539:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  financially  quite  sophisticated.   Sizeable  spreads  exist,  on  average,  between  different
3:73:4621:18:18:71:539:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rates;  moreover, these spreads are not constant over time, especially in periods of
3:74:4714:18:18:71:539:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial stress.  And “tighter” financial conditions, indicated by increases in the size of credit
3:75:4813:18:18:71:539:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads, are commonly associated with lower levels of real expenditure and employment. This
3:76:4904:18:18:71:539:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:poses obvious questions for the practical application of much work in the theory of monetary
3:77:4996:18:18:71:539:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy.3If  a  model  is  to  be  calibrated  or  estimated  using  time  series  data,  which  actual
3:78:5098:18:18:71:539:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rate should be taken to correspond to “the interest rate” in the model?  When the
3:79:5188:18:18:71:539:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model is used to to give advice about how interest rates should respond to a particular type
3:80:5280:18:17:71:539:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of shock, which actual interest rate (if any) should be made to respond in the way that “the
3:81:5372:17:18:71:539:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rate” does in the model?  How large an error is likely to be made by abstracting from
3:82:5466:18:18:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit frictions, with regard to the model’s predictions for the variables that appear in it?
3:83:5559:18:18:71:539:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover, some questions clearly cannot even be addressed using models that abstract from
3:84:5648:18:18:71:539:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit frictions.  Most notably, how should a central bank respond to a “financial shock” that
3:85:5742:18:18:71:393:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increases the size of the spreads resulting from credit frictions?
3:86:5808:18:18:89:539:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This paper seeks to address these questions by presenting a simple extension of the basic
3:87:5897:18:12:85:534:119:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:1See, for example,Clarida, Gali and Gertler(1999) orWoodford(2003), among many other references.
3:88:5993:12:12:85:480:107:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:2The models ofSmets and Wouters(2003,2007) provide an especially influential example.
3:89:6078:12:15:85:539:95:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:3The pre-crisis generation of DSGE models was criticized on this ground byIssing(2006) andGoodhart
3:90:6176:15:0:71:166:80:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:(2007), among others.
4:91:6242:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“New Keynesian” model (as developed, for example, in Woodford,2003) in which a credit
4:92:6327:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:friction is introduced, allowing for a time-varying wedge between the interest rate available to
4:93:6423:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:households on their savings and the interest rate at which it is possible to borrow.  Financial
4:94:6518:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediation matters for the allocation of resources due to the introduction of heterogeneity
4:95:6613:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the spending opportunities currently available to different households.  While the model
4:96:6704:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:remains  highly  stylized,  it  has  the  advantage  of  nesting  the  basic  New  Keynesian  model
4:97:6803:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(extensively used in normative monetary policy analysis) as a special case, and of introducing
4:98:6897:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only  a  small  number  of  additional  parameters,  the  consequences  of  which  for  conclusions
4:99:6996:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about  the  monetary  transmission  mechanism  and  the  character  of  optimal  policy  can  be
4:100:7092:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thoroughly explored.  The approach taken also seeks to develop a tractable model, with as
4:101:7181:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small a state space as is consistent with an allowance for financial frictions and heterogeneity,
4:102:7278:18:18:72:496:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and hence only modestly greater complexity than the basic New Keynesian model.
4:103:7356:18:17:89:539:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Among the questions to be addressed are the following:  If the parameters determining
4:104:7441:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the degree of heterogeneity and the size of credit frictions are calibrated so as to match both
4:105:7536:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the volume of bank credit and the spread between bank deposit and lending rates in the US
4:106:7625:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy, how much of a difference does this make (relative to the frictionless baseline) for
4:107:7717:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model’s predictions for the response of the economy to various types of shocks, under a
4:108:7808:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:given monetary policy rule?  How much of a difference does it make for the implied responses
4:109:7900:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  real  disturbances  under  an  optimal  monetary  policy?   How  much  of  a  difference  does
4:110:7998:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it make for the form of the quadratic stabilization objective that would correspond to the
4:111:8088:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:maximization of average expected utility?  How much of a difference does it make for the
4:112:8176:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:form  of  the  optimal  target  criterion  for  monetary  stabilization  policy?   And  how  should
4:113:8275:18:18:72:319:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy optimally respond to a “financial shock”?
4:114:8323:18:18:89:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The model also provides perspective on “rules of thumb” for policy in times of financial
4:115:8411:18:18:72:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turmoil  proposed  in  the  recent  literature.   For  example,McCulley  and  Toloui(2008)  and
4:116:8506:18:18:71:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Taylor(2008) propose that the intercept term in a “Taylor rule” for monetary policy should
4:117:8596:18:17:71:539:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be adjusted downward in proportion to observed increases in spreads.4Here we use our simple
4:118:8687:17:18:71:539:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model to ask whether it is correct to say that the “natural” or “neutral” rate of interest is
4:119:8780:18:18:71:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower when credit spreads increase (assuming unchanged fundamentals otherwise),  and to
4:120:8867:18:18:71:539:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the extent that it is, how the size of the change in the natural rate compares to the size of
4:121:8960:18:18:71:539:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the change in credit spreads.  We also ask whether it is approximately correct to say that
4:122:9050:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a proper response to a “financial shock” is to conduct policy according to the same rule as
4:123:9141:18:16:85:539:113:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:4Similarly, Meyer and Sack (2008) propose, as a possible account of recent U.S. Federal Reserve policy,
4:124:9244:16:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a Taylor rule in which the intercept—representing the Fed’s view of “the equilibrium real funds rate”—has
4:125:9349:12:12:72:540:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:been adjusted downward in response to credit market turmoil,  and use the size of increases in spreads in
4:126:9454:12:0:72:414:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:early 2008 as a basis for a proposed magnitude of the appropriate adjustment.
5:127:9576:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:under other circumstances, except with the operating target for the policy rate adjusted by a
5:128:9669:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:factor that is proportional to the increase in credit spreads; and again, to the extent that such
5:129:9766:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an approximation is used, we ask what proportion of adjustment should be made.  C ́urdia
5:130:9854:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Woodford  (2010)  use  the  framework  presented  in  this  paper  to  evaluate  the  positive
5:131:9953:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and normative consequences of adopting the proposals of McCulley and Toloui(2008) and
5:132:10038:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Taylor(2008) and find that an adjustment for variations in credit spreads can improve upon
5:133:10128:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the standard Taylor rule, but the optimal size (and direction) of adjustment depends on the
5:134:10219:18:18:72:278:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:source of the variation in credit spreads.
5:135:10261:18:18:89:539:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Other  authors  have  argued  that  if  financial  disturbances  are  an  important  source  of
5:136:10356:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:macroeconomic instability, a sound approach to monetary policy will have to pay attention
5:137:10445:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  the  balance  sheets  of  financial  intermediaries.   It  is  sometimes  suggested  that  policy
5:138:10546:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:should  respond  to  variations  in  the  growth  rate  of  monetary  or  credit  aggregates,  rather
5:139:10647:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than — as in the case of both the Taylor rule and conventional prescriptions for “flexible
5:140:10737:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation  targeting”  —  seeking  to  determine  the  appropriate  level  of  short-term  interest
5:141:10836:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates purely on the basis of observations of or projections for measures of inflation and real
5:142:10930:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:activity.  Here we consider two possible interpretations of such proposals:  as an argument
5:143:11021:18:18:72:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fortargetingmonetary  and/or  credit  aggregates,  or  at  least  adopting  a  target  criterion
5:144:11117:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  involves  such  variables  along  with  others;  or  as  an  argument  for  their  special  value
5:145:11220:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asindicators,so that such variables should receive substantial weight in the central bank’s
5:146:11311:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reaction  function.   We  address  the  first  issue  by  deriving  an  optimal  target  criterion  for
5:147:11414:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy, under certain simplifying assumptions, and seeing to what extent it involves
5:148:11507:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:either money or credit.  We address the second issue, under assumptions that are arguably
5:149:11596:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more  realistic,  by  computing  the  optimal  responses  to  shocks,  and  asking  what  kinds  of
5:150:11695:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indicator variables would allow a simple rule of thumb to bring about equilibrium responses
5:151:11786:18:18:72:134:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of this kind.
5:152:11799:18:18:89:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Of course, we are not the first to investigate ways in which New Keynesian [NK] models
5:153:11885:18:17:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be extended to allow for financial frictions of one type or another.  A number of authors
5:154:11978:17:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have analyzed DSGE models with financial frictions of one type or another before the recent
5:155:12069:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial crisis.5Many of the best-known contributions introduce obstacles to the willingness
5:156:12162:18:16:85:539:167:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:5Probably the most influential early example was the model ofBernanke, Gertler and Gilchrist(1999).
5:157:12261:16:12:72:539:151:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:More recent contributions includeChristiano, Motto and Rostagno(2003,2010),Christiano et al.(2008),
5:158:12360:12:12:72:540:139:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Gertler,  Gilchrist  and  Natalucci(2007),  andIacoviello(2005).Faia  and  Monacelli(2007)  consider  how
5:159:12465:12:12:71:539:127:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:two  different  types  of  financial  frictions  affect  welfare-based policy  evaluation,  though  from  a  perspective
5:160:12585:12:12:71:539:115:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:somewhat different than the one taken here; they compare alternative simple rules, rather than computing
5:161:12689:12:12:71:539:103:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:optimal  policy,  as  we  do,  and  compute  the  welfare  associated  with  a  particular  rule  under  a  complete
5:162:12805:12:12:71:539:91:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:specification  of  shocks,  rather  than  considering  what  a  given  simple  rule  implies  about  the  equilibrium
5:163:12922:12:0:71:539:79:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:responses  to  shocks  considered  individually.C ́urdia(2008)  considers  optimal  policy  in  the  spirit  of  the
6:164:13083:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of savers to lend to borrowers, but assume that borrowers directly borrow from the suppliers
6:165:13175:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of savings.  The recent financial crisis increased interest in models like ours that explicitly
6:166:13270:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:introduce intermediaries and allow for a spread between the interest received by savers and
6:167:13361:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  paid  by  borrowers;  early  contributions  includeHulsewig,  Mayer  and  Wollmershauser
6:168:13455:18:18:72:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:(2009),Teranishi(2008),Sudo and Teranishi(2008), andGerali, Neri and Signoretti(2008).6
6:169:13542:18:18:89:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:More  recently,Gertler  and  Kiyotaki(2010)  also  seek  to  provide  a  canonical  model  of
6:170:13635:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit market frictions and economic activity.  Their work extends the “financial accelerator”
6:171:13729:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:framework to the case in which financial intermediaries themselves are exposed to the risk of
6:172:13822:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:default and thus face constraints on their ability to attract deposits (unlikeBernanke, Gertler
6:173:13917:18:18:72:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Gilchrist,1999).  Gertler and Kiyotaki use this model to discuss the consequences to
6:174:14005:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real activity in the case of an imperfect interbank market, in which the banks cannot fully
6:175:14096:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:offset their risk exposure by pooling their loans.  Their analysis is similar in spirit to ours
6:176:14191:18:17:72:539:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but less focused on monetary policy.  Related recent contributions include those ofMeh and
6:177:14281:17:18:72:474:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moran(2010),Kiyotaki and Moore(2012), andJermann and Quadrini(2012).
6:178:14349:18:18:89:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In general,  these models are fairly complex,  in the interest of microfoundation and/or
6:179:14437:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantitative realism, and the results obtained are mostly numerical.  Our aim here is some-
6:180:14528:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what different.  While the interest of such analyses is clear, especially to policy institutions
6:181:14624:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:seeking quantitative estimates of the effects of particular contemplated actions, we believe
6:182:14716:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that it is also valuable to seek analytical insights of the kind that can only be obtained from
6:183:14811:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analyses of simpler, more stylized models.  Here we focus on the consequences for monetary
6:184:14901:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy analysis of two basic features of economies — heterogeneity of non-financial economic
6:185:14993:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:units, of a kind that gives the financial sector a non-trivial role in the allocation of resources;
6:186:15092:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and costs of financial intermediation, that may be subject to random variation for reasons
6:187:15182:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relating largely to developments in the financial sector — in the simplest possible setting,
6:188:15274:18:18:72:434:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where we do not introduce other departures from the basic NK model.
6:189:15341:18:18:89:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Two  contributions  have  aims  more  closely  related  to  ours.   Like  us,Goodfriend  and
6:190:15433:18:17:72:539:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:McCallum(2007) consider a fairly simple NK model, with new model elements limited to
6:191:15517:17:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those necessary to allow for multiple interest rates with different average levels (including,
6:192:15611:18:18:72:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:like us,  a distinction between bank lending rates and the policy rate).7As in the present
6:193:15701:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:paper, a primary goal is to “investigate quantitatively how much a central bank can be misled
6:194:15794:18:22:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by relying on a [NK] model without money and banking when managing its interbank-rate
6:195:15879:22:9:72:499:127:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:present paper, but in a more complex model with features specific to emerging-market economies.
6:196:15974:9:15:85:540:118:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:6See Gerali, Neri and Signoretti(2008, sec.  2) for a more detailed discussion of early work in this vein.
6:197:16080:15:12:72:540:103:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:See alsoBrunnermeier,  Eisenbach and Sannikov(2012) for a very extensive survey of the macroeconomic
6:198:16180:12:9:72:307:91:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:implications of financial frictions of a variety of types.
6:199:16238:9:0:85:515:82:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:7This paper provides a quantitative analysis of type of model first proposed byGoodfriend(2005).
7:200:16379:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy instrument.”  De Fiore and Tristani (2011) also propose a simple generalization of the
7:201:16472:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:basic NK model in order to introduce a distinction between loan rates and the policy; also
7:202:16562:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:like us, they consider how financial frictions affect the “natural rate of interest,” and the role
7:203:16660:18:18:72:482:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of such a concept in inflation determination in an economy with credit frictions.
7:204:16741:18:18:89:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The approaches taken by these authors nonetheless differ from ours in important respects.
7:205:16830:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In particular, unlike us, Goodfriend and McCallum assume a representative-household model;
7:206:16920:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as a consequence, financial intermediation matters for resource allocation in their model only
7:207:17014:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because they assume that certain liabilities of banks (transactions balances) play a crucial
7:208:17106:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:role in facilitating transactions.  We instead treat the fact that some (but not all) financial
7:209:17201:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries finance (some) of their lending by providing accounts that are useful as means
7:210:17294:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of payment as inessential to the primary function of financial intermediaries in the economy;
7:211:17387:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and in our model, for the sake of simplicity, we assume that intermediaries finance themselves
7:212:17481:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entirely by issuing deposits that supply no transactions services at all (so that in equilibrium,
7:213:17578:17:18:72:392:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deposits must pay the same interest rate as government debt).
7:214:17639:18:18:89:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:De Fiore and Tristani instead have two types of infinite-lived agents (“households” and
7:215:17726:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“entrepreneurs,” following Bernanke, Gertler and Gilchrist (1999), one of which saves while
7:216:17817:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  other  borrows;  but  in  their  model,  unlike  ours,  agents  belong  permanently  to  one  of
7:217:17918:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these categories, and one is tempted to identify the division between them with the division
7:218:18010:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between  households  and  firms  in  the  flow  of  funds  accounts.   This  would  be  desirable,  of
7:219:18112:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:course,  if one thought that the model did adequately capture the nature of that division,
7:220:18202:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the model would yield additional testable predictions.  But in fact, there are both saving
7:221:18295:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:units and borrowing units at a given point in time, both in the household sector and in the
7:222:18386:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm sector; and a saving unit at one point in time need not be a saving unit forever.  We
7:223:18476:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accordingly prefer not to introduce a distinction between households and firms (or “house-
7:224:18566:18:18:72:540:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:holds” and “entrepreneurs”) at all, and also not to assume that the identities of our savers
7:225:18658:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  borrowers  are  permanent.8In  addition,  De  Fiore  and  Tristani,  like  Goodfriend  and
7:226:18753:18:17:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:McCallum, assume that money must be used in (some) transactions, while we abstract from
7:227:18840:17:18:72:471:203:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:transactions frictions of this kind altogether in order to simplify our analysis.9
7:228:18922:18:16:85:539:185:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:8In fact, De Fiore and Tristani list as an important “undesirable property” of their model the fact that
7:229:19026:16:12:72:540:169:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in  it,  “households  and  entrepreneurs  are  radically  different  agents”  (p.   23),  as  the  predicted  equilibrium
7:230:19147:12:12:72:540:157:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:behavior of “households” as a group does not look much like that of the aggregate household sector in actual
7:231:19255:12:8:72:119:145:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:economies.
7:232:19265:8:16:85:539:137:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:9Goodfriend and McCallum justify the introduction of a cash-in-advance constraint in their model, stating
7:233:19370:16:12:72:540:121:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:(footnote 6) that “medium-of-exchange money is implicitly central to our analysis because it is by managing
7:234:19477:12:12:72:540:109:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the aggregate quantity of reserves, which banks hold to facilitate transactions, that monetary policy affects
7:235:19586:12:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:interest  rates.”   However,  while  in  their  model,  banks  hold  reserves  at  the  central  bank  only  because  of
7:236:19706:12:12:72:540:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a reserve requirement proportional to transactions balances,  this need not be true in actual economies,  a
7:237:19813:12:0:72:540:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:number of which (such as Canada) have abolished reserve requirements.  Moreover, it is possible in principle
8:238:19966:0:18:89:539:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:With  the  extensive  use  of  unconventional  policies  by  central  banks  across  the  world
8:239:20061:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  response  to  the  financial  crisis,  models  such  as  the  one  we  discuss  have  been  called  to
8:240:20167:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evaluate those policies.  That goes beyond the scope of this paper.  C ́urdia and Woodford
8:241:20257:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2011)  extend  our  framework  to  explicitly  evaluate  the  use  of  the  central  bank’s  balance
8:242:20358:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sheet to stabilize the economy,  namely through “credit policy” — the purchase of illiquid
8:243:20448:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets by the central bank.Gertler and Karadi(2011) also analyze the use of “credit policy”
8:244:20539:18:18:72:344:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:through an extension ofGertler and Kiyotaki(2010).
8:245:20589:18:18:89:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We develop our model in section2, and compare its structure with that of the basic NK
8:246:20674:18:18:71:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model.   We  then  consider,  in  section3,  the  implications  of  the  model  for  the  equilibrium
8:247:20775:18:18:71:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects  of  a  variety  of  types  of  exogenous  disturbances,  under  a  given  assumption  about
8:248:20875:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy (such as that it conform to a “Taylor rule”), and ask to what extent the
8:249:20963:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:basic  NK  model  gives  incorrect  answers  to  these  questions.   Section4  considers  optimal
8:250:21060:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy in the context of our model, defined to mean a policy that maximizes the
8:251:21148:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average  expected  utility  of  households,  and  again  considers  how  different  the  conclusions
8:252:21248:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  from  those  derived  from  the  basic  NK  model.   We  also  discuss  the  way  in  which  the
8:253:21349:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest-rate  reaction  function  required  to  implement  a  “flexible  inflation  target”  should
8:254:21449:18:45:72:519:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:involve responses to variations in credit spreads.  Section5 summarizes our conclusions.
8:255:21537:45:30:72:521:355:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    A New Keynesian Model with Financial Frictions
8:256:21588:30:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here we sketch a model that introduces heterogeneity of the kind needed in order for financial
8:257:21682:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediation to matter for resource allocation, and a limit on the degree of intermediation
8:258:21775:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that occurs in equilibrium, with a minimum of structure.  We stress the similarity between
8:259:21865:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model presented here and the basic New Keynesian model, and show how the standard
8:260:21950:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model  is  recovered  as  a  special  case  of  the  one  developed  here.   This  sets  the  stage  for  a
8:261:22057:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantitative investigation of the degree to which credit frictions of an empirically realistic
8:262:22151:18:21:72:316:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:magnitude change the predictions of the model.
8:263:22197:21:12:72:540:196:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:for a central bank to control the interest rate in the interbank market for central-bank deposits without there
8:264:22308:12:12:72:540:184:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:being any demand for such reservesotherthan as a riskless store of value, as discussed inWoodford(2003,
8:265:22411:12:12:72:540:172:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:chap.  2).  Hence there is no need to introduce a demand for money for transactions purposes in our model,
8:266:22517:12:12:72:540:160:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in order for it to be possible to suppose that the central bank controls a short-term nominal interest rate,
8:267:22625:12:0:72:373:148:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:that will correspond to the rate at which banks can fund themselves.
9:268:22738:0:26:72:412:687:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.1    Financial Frictions and Aggregate Demand
9:269:22785:26:18:72:540:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  depart  from  the  assumption  of  a  representative  household  in  the  standard  model,  by
9:270:22883:18:18:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:supposing that households differ in their preferences.  Each householdiseeks to maximize a
9:271:22973:18:38:72:311:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discounted intertemporal objective of the form
9:272:23019:38:0:172:184:587:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f4:?:E0
9:273:23021:0:28:191:204:602:8:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f11:?:∞∑

10:321:26511:18:18:89:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The coexistence of the two types with differing impatience to consume creates a social

10:338:27999:8:16:81:539:220:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:14The “consumption” variable is therefore to be interpreted as representing all of private expenditure, not
10:339:28106:16:12:72:540:204:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:only consumer expenditure.  In reality, one of the most important reasons for some economic units to wish

10:343:28528:12:12:72:540:156:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:expenditure for future productivity.  For discussion of the interpretation of “consumption” in the basic New
10:344:28636:12:8:72:302:144:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Keynesian model, seeWoodford(2003, pp.  242-243).
10:345:28685:8:15:81:539:136:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:15Here “savers” and “borrowers” identify households according to whether they choose to save or borrow,

16:554:42596:18:18:72:540:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relating that marginal utility of income to the expected real rate of return implied by the
16:555:42687:18:18:72:540:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model’s single interest rate.  The present model implies a similar relation between interest
16:556:42779:18:18:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates and the timing of expenditure as in the basic model.  The main differences are (i) that
16:557:42872:18:18:72:540:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:now there aretwo differentinterest rates that each affect aggregate demand (though with

16:559:43051:18:18:72:482:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the resources used by the banking sector can also affect aggregate demand.
16:560:43130:18:18:89:539:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The presence of two interest rates relevant to aggregate demand determination does not
16:561:43216:18:18:72:540:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mean there are two independent dimensions of monetary policy.  Instead, the two rates must
16:562:43306:18:18:72:539:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be linked by equations (2.7)–(2.8), determining the equilibrium credit spread.21If we intro-
16:563:43398:18:17:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duce no further frictions, the policy rate (which is a rate at which banks are willing to lend

16:565:43580:18:18:72:539:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  the  central  bank  directly  controls  this  rate.23In  the  case  that  banking  uses  no  real
16:566:43683:18:18:72:539:269:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f12:B:resources (so that Ξt(bt) = 0 regardless of the volume of lending) and the credit spreadωt
16:567:43773:18:18:72:539:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is purely exogenous (i.e.,independent of the volume of lending),24the system consisting of
16:568:43863:18:19:72:540:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equations (2.7)–(2.8) and (2.12)–(2.15) gives a complete account of how real aggregate de-
16:569:43953:19:15:81:539:214:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:21Of course, thereisan additional, independent dimension of central-bank policy if the central bank has
16:570:44056:15:12:72:540:199:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:measures, independent of its control of the policy rate, that can influence the financial frictions represented
16:571:44167:12:9:72:507:187:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:by the functions Ξt(bt) orχt(bt) introduced in the next section.  We leave this issue for future work.
16:572:44269:9:15:81:539:178:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:22We could introduce a distinction between the rate that banks pay depositors and the rate banks pay

16:575:44573:12:8:72:451:139:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:borrowing funds in the interbank market.  We abstract from reserve requirements here.
16:576:44658:8:16:81:539:131:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:23The issues involved in discussing how the central bank actually controls the policy rate are no different

17:604:47190:39:25:72:284:253:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.2    The Intermediary Sector
17:605:47220:25:18:72:540:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here we further explain our assumptions about the behavior of intermediaries and the de-
17:606:47308:18:18:72:539:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terminants of the equilibrium credit spreadωt.  We allow for two sources of credit spreads
17:607:47398:18:18:72:540:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:—  one  of  which  follows  from  an  assumption  that  intermediation  requires  real  resources,
17:608:47496:18:18:72:540:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the other of which does not — which provide two distinct sources of “purely financial”
17:609:47586:18:18:72:208:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances in our model.
17:610:47612:18:18:89:539:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First, we assume that real resources Ξt(bt) are consumed in the process of originating loans
17:611:47704:18:16:81:539:120:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:25To be more precise, the expected path of real interest rates determines only desired current expenditure
17:612:47810:16:12:72:540:104:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:relative to expected future expenditure, so that current aggregate demand also depends on expected long-run
17:613:47917:12:12:72:540:92:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:output, just as in the basic NK model (see,e.g.,Woodford,2003, chap.  4).  The expected long-run level of
17:614:48022:12:8:72:423:80:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:output is determined by supply-side factors and by the long-run inflation target.
17:615:48103:8:0:81:281:72:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:26See the Appendix for demonstration of this.
18:616:48194:0:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of real quantitybt, and that these resources must be produced and consumed in the period
18:617:48282:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in which the loans are originated.27The function Ξt(bt) is assumed to be non-decreasing and
18:618:48373:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at least weakly convex.  Strict convexity of Ξt(b) would indicate increasing costs owing to a
18:619:48466:18:18:72:410:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capacity constraint, e.g.  the scarcity of available managerial time.
18:620:48535:18:18:89:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In addition, we suppose that in order to originate a quantity of loansbtthat will be repaid
18:621:48626:18:18:71:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(with interest) in the following period,  it is necessary for an  intermediary to also make a
18:622:48719:18:18:71:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantityχt(bt) of loans that will be defaulted upon, whereχt(bt) is also a non-decreasing,
18:623:48809:18:18:71:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weakly convex function.  (This function may also be strictly convex, due to reduced accuracy
18:624:48901:18:18:71:465:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of screening the larger the volume of lending relative to the bank’s capacity.)
18:625:48980:18:18:89:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We assume that the bank cannot tell the legitimate borrowers and fraudulent borrowers
18:626:49065:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:apart,  and so must treat them equally.  However,  the bank is able to predict the fraction
18:627:49156:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of its loans that will turn out to be fraudulent, and so correctly predicts that loan repay-
18:628:49248:18:0:71:277:471:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f12:B:ments in periodt+ 1 will total onlyPtbt
18:629:49287:0:10:279:284:481:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:?:(

18:631:49294:0:10:313:318:481:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:?:)
18:632:49295:10:17:319:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:, even though the loans extended had value
18:633:49337:17:18:71:540:454:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:Pt[bt+χt(bt)].  The fact that the same interest rate must be charged for both types of loans
18:634:49429:18:18:71:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:means that the existence of the default risk increases the cost of financing projects that are
18:635:49523:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:known to the borrower to be riskless; so a credit spread due to this kind of risk represents
18:636:49615:18:18:71:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a barrier to efficient financial intermediation.  The opportunity to make a fraudulent loan
18:637:49706:18:18:71:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contract is assumed to arrive randomly to each household with equal probability, regardless
18:638:49797:18:18:71:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the household’s current type.  Thus each household has additional real income each period

18:643:50232:18:18:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of its loans (anticipating that a certain fraction of the loans will not be repaid).  Any excess
18:644:50328:18:18:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:funds received from depositors that are not lent out or used to pay the resource costs of loan

19:687:52910:12:9:72:432:166:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:income depend on activity in the intermediary sector, though for different reasons.
19:688:52993:9:15:81:539:157:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:29Certainly we do not deny that at least at certain times, central banks do seek to affect the efficiency of
19:689:53101:15:12:72:540:142:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the banking system; this is true most obviously in the case of actions taken in a central bank’s capacity as
19:690:53209:12:12:72:540:130:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:“lender of last resort” during a financial crisis.  However, we regard such actions as representing a largely
19:691:53318:12:12:72:540:118:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f7:F:independentdimension of policy frommonetarypolicy, by which we mean control of the supply of central-
19:692:53419:12:12:72:540:106:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:bank  balances  to  the  payments  system,  and  of  the  overnight  interest  rate  paid  for  such  balances  in  the
19:693:53538:12:12:72:540:94:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:interbank market.  (Additional lending to intermediaries through the discount window or similar facilities
19:694:53644:12:12:72:540:82:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:need not imply any increase in the total supply of central-bank deposits, as the actions of the Federal Reserve
19:695:53755:12:0:72:540:70:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:between September 2007 and September 2008 illustrated.)  Here we are concerned solely with the analysis
20:696:53904:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects of monetary policy, and for the optimal conduct of monetary policy, of the existence
20:697:53996:18:39:72:505:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of, and of exogenous variation in, obstacles to fully efficient financial intermediation.

24:855:62503:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ables, in order to have a complete general-equilibrium model of the monetary transmission
24:856:62592:18:18:72:132:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism.
24:857:62602:18:18:89:539:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A  noteworthy  property  of  this  system  is  that  when  credit  frictions  matter,  Ricardian
24:858:62698:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equivalence generally does not obtain.  Even if we consider alternative paths for{bgt}while
24:859:62789:18:18:72:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:holding the path of distorting taxes{τt}constant, so that contemplated changes in the path
24:860:62879:18:18:71:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of government debt are achieved entirely through changes in the size of lump-sum transfers, a
24:861:62972:18:18:71:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:change in the path of the public debtwillgenerally require a different equilibrium evolution

24:863:63169:18:18:71:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model.33For  (2.27)  implies  that  in  the  absence  of  any  offsetting  changes  in  the  paths  of
24:864:63271:18:18:71:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other endogenous variables, a change in the path of{bgt}will require an offsetting change
24:865:63360:18:18:71:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the path of{bt}; essentially, government borrowing crowds out private borrowing, in the
24:866:63450:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:absence  of  changes  in  macroeconomic  conditions  that  increase  aggregate  private  saving.34
24:867:63548:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  the  special  case  considered  at  the  end  of  the  previous  section  (when  Ξt=  0  andωtis
24:868:63648:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:independent of the level of private debt), this change in the path of private indebtedness still
24:869:63744:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has no consequences for the determination of aggregate output, interest rates or inflation,
24:870:63835:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or  for  the  allocation  of  consumption  or  labor  effort  between  the  two  types  of  households,
24:871:63938:18:18:72:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and so Ricardian equivalence still obtains.  However,exceptin this special case, a change in
24:872:64030:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the path of private indebtedness has consequences for aggregate demand determination, by
24:873:64118:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changing the spread between the lending rate and the deposit rate, by changing the resources
24:874:64210:18:39:72:235:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used by intermediaries, or both.
24:875:64242:39:25:72:235:307:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.4    Aggregate Supply
24:876:64265:25:18:72:540:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:It remains to specify the aggregate supply side of the model.  This part of the model remains
24:877:64358:18:18:72:540:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  same  as  the  basic  NK  model  (as  expounded,  for  example,  in  Benigno  and  Woodford,
24:878:64455:18:18:72:540:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2005), except that in modelling the cost of supplying a given quantity of output (and hence
24:879:64546:18:16:81:539:228:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:33Crucial to this result is our assumption here that the government can borrow from the private sector at a
24:880:64653:16:12:72:539:212:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:rate more favorable than that available to private non-financial borrowers: the rateidtat which intermediaries
24:881:64763:12:12:72:540:200:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:are able to obtain funding, rather than the rateibtpaid by households that must borrow from intermediaries.
24:882:64870:12:12:72:540:188:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:In effect, when the public debt is increased the government is (among other things) borrowing at this lower
24:883:64977:12:12:72:540:176:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:rate on behalf of households that would like to borrow at this rate but are assumed to be unable to do so
24:884:65082:12:12:72:540:164:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:on their own account.  This increases aggregate demand in somewhat the same way as a reduction in credit
24:885:65186:12:8:72:129:152:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:spreads does.
24:886:65199:8:16:81:539:144:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:34In the simple case in whichωt(bt) = Ξt(bt) = 0,(2.27) determines the evolution of an aggregate credit
24:887:65302:16:12:71:540:128:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:variable,bt+πbbgt, in a way that is independent of the composition of that variable, so that a unit increase in
24:888:65413:12:12:71:540:116:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f7:F:bgtrequires a reduction ofbtby preciselyπbunits, so that each borrowing household must borrow exactly one
24:889:65518:12:12:72:540:104:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:unit less for each unit that is borrowed (per capita) by the government.  The relation between the evolution
24:890:65626:12:12:72:540:92:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of the two variables is more complex when private indebtedness increases credit frictions while government
24:891:65732:12:11:72:540:80:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:debt does not, but the most important effect of government borrowing remains the “crowding out” of private
24:892:65838:11:0:72:119:69:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:borrowing.
25:893:65894:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  incentives  of  price-setters)  we  must  take  account  of  the  differing  labor  supply  behav-
25:894:65997:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ior of savers and borrowers.  The model of labor supply explained above implies that the

25:920:67289:18:18:71:539:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the relations (2.29) reduce to exactly the ones inBenigno and Woodford(2005).  The system
25:921:67378:18:18:71:539:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2.28)–(2.29) indicates the nature of the short-run aggregate-supply trade-off between infla-

25:925:67756:17:18:71:540:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and (2.28)–(2.29), together with equations specifying interest-rate policy and the evolution

25:927:67937:18:18:71:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endogenous variables{Yt,λbt,λst,ibt,idt,zt,Πt,∆t,bt}, given the evolution of the exogenous dis-
25:928:68032:18:0:71:124:126:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turbances.
26:929:68088:0:30:72:542:687:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:F:3    Credit Frictions and the Propagation of Disturbances
26:930:68145:30:18:72:540:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We have shown that it is possible to generalize the basic NK model in a fairly straightforward
26:931:68239:18:18:72:540:639:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:way to incorporate credit frictions — more specifically, a spread between the deposit rate
26:932:68329:18:18:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  the  lending  rate,  that  may  be  large  or  small,  constant  or  variable,  and  exogenous  or
26:933:68432:18:18:72:540:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endogenous, depending how we choose to parameterize the model.  This shows, at the very
26:934:68519:18:18:72:540:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:least, that the inherent structure of NK models does not in some way require one to ignore the
26:935:68613:18:18:72:540:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:existence of such frictions.  But how much does this generalization change the implications
26:936:68704:18:18:72:190:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the resulting model?
26:937:68727:18:18:89:539:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this section, we consider the effects on the economy of a variety of types of exogenous
26:938:68817:18:18:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances, including monetary policy shocks, under simple specifications of monetary pol-
26:939:68909:18:17:72:540:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:icy.  Our goal is not yet to compare monetary policies, but rather to compare the predictions
26:940:69002:17:18:72:540:478:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  alternative  model  specifications;  we  wish  to  determine  to  what  extent  our  conclusions
26:941:69102:18:18:72:540:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about the consequences of a given monetary policy are affected by the introduction of het-
26:942:69192:18:39:72:228:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:erogeneity and credit frictions.
26:943:69224:39:26:72:362:403:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.1    Log-Linearized Structural Relations
26:944:69266:26:18:72:540:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To  approach  this  question,  we  log-linearize  the  structural  relations  of  our  model  around
26:945:69366:18:18:72:540:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:steady-state  values  of  the  various  endogenous  variables  that  represent  a  perfect  foresight
26:946:69467:18:18:72:540:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium  in  the  case  of  no  random  variation  in  any  of  the  exogenous  disturbance  pro-
26:947:69568:18:18:72:540:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cesses, as discussed further in the Appendix.  The solution to these linear equations under a
26:948:69661:18:18:72:540:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correspondingly log-linear specification of monetary policy provides a linear approximation
26:949:69752:18:18:72:540:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  the  equilibrium  responses  to  the  various  types  of  disturbances,  in  the  case  that  these
26:950:69855:18:17:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:random variations are small enough.  The linearity of the solution allows us to discuss the
26:951:69946:17:18:72:540:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium responses to individual shocks independently of whether other exogenous vari-
26:952:70035:18:18:72:540:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ables change concurrently, and to discuss the size of the responses relative to the size of the
26:953:70130:18:18:72:418:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shock without caring about the size of the shock that is considered.
26:954:70198:18:18:89:539:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We first summarize the structure of the log-linearized model, as these equations them-
26:955:70284:18:18:72:540:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selves  provide  considerable  insight  into  the  model’s  implications,  and  the  similarities  and
26:956:70386:18:18:72:540:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differences  between  the  predictions  of  the  generalized  model  and  those  of  the  basic  NK
26:957:70485:18:18:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model (which is itself most familiar in its log-linearized form).  We log-linearize the struc-
26:958:70579:18:18:72:540:126:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tural relations of the previous section around a steady state with zero inflation ( ̄Π = 1).  This
26:959:70677:18:18:72:540:108:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:means that in our analysis, we shall restrict attention to monetary policy rules that imply
26:960:70768:18:18:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an inflation rate of zero, or one not far from zero, in the absence of stochastic disturbances.
26:961:70863:18:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This simplification is familiar in the standard NK literature, and we follow it here in order
27:962:71002:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to focus solely on the new complications introduced by heterogeneity and credit frictions.
27:963:71092:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover, we show in section 3 that according to the present model, optimal monetary policy
27:964:71183:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has this property; hence the approximation adopted here suffices for the study of monetary
27:965:71273:18:18:72:317:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policies that are close enough to optimal policy.

30:1094:78442:26:18:72:540:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here the composite exogenous disturbance termˆYnt(the “natural rate of output”) is a linear
30:1095:78533:18:18:72:540:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:combination of the disturbances  ̄ct,ˆGt, ̄ht,andˆZt(sources of variation in the flexible-price

31:1098:78864:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:3); the additional exogenous termut(the “cost-push shock”) is instead a linear combination
31:1099:78954:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the disturbances  ˆμwtand  ˆτt(sources of variation in the flexible-price equilibrium level of
31:1100:79051:18:18:72:539:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:output that donotcorrespond to any change in the efficient level of output).  This is identi-
31:1101:79144:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cal to the “new Keynesian Phillips curve” of the basic NK model, with the exception of the
31:1102:79234:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terms proportional toˆΩtandˆΞt, indicating “cost-push” effects of the credit frictions in our
31:1103:79327:18:18:72:156:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:extended model.
31:1104:79342:18:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Equations (3.8) and (3.12) are thus direct analogs of two of the equations of the canonical
31:1105:79433:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“three-equation  model”;  the  third  equation  (a  central-bank  reaction  function,  such  as  a
31:1106:79531:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Taylor rule, for the policy rate as a function of inflation and output) is unchanged by the
31:1107:79622:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:existence of credit frictions.  In the case that both{ˆωt}and{ˆΞt}can be treated as exogenous
31:1108:79715:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:processes (so that{ˆΩt}is exogenous as well),  these same three equations again provide a
31:1109:79804:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complete system for the determination of equilibrium inflation,  output and interest rates,
31:1110:79895:18:17:71:539:471:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:exceptthat one must adjoin equation (3.10) to connect the interest rate that appears in the
31:1111:79986:17:18:71:538:454:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f12:B:IS relation to the policy rate.  If one substitutes the central-bank reaction function for ˆıdt
31:1112:80081:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in (3.10),  in order to derive the implied response of the average interest rate — or if one
31:1113:80173:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:supposes that the central bank uses the average interest rate as its operating target, a policy
31:1114:80268:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proposal  that  we  analyze  further  in  section  3  —  then  one  again  obtains  a  three-equation
31:1115:80369:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model directly analogous to the basic NK model.  For example, if the central bank follows a
31:1116:80460:18:18:72:189:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Taylor rule of the form
31:1117:80483:18:26:248:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆıdt=φππt+φyˆYt+-mt,(3.13)
31:1118:80509:26:33:72:376:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then the complete model would consist of (3.8), (3.12), and

31:1120:80602:33:17:72:540:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The only differences relative to the basic NK model are that the interest rate appearing in
31:1121:80693:17:18:72:540:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this three-equation system is not the only relevant interest rate and may not correspond to
31:1122:80784:18:18:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the policy rate; that the numerical values of the coefficients  ̄σandκmust take appropriate
31:1123:80875:18:18:72:540:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:account of the different degrees of interest-sensitivity of expenditure of different units in the
31:1124:80972:18:18:72:540:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy;  and that time-varying financial frictions are an additional source of disturbance
31:1125:81063:18:18:72:216:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terms in all three equations.
31:1126:81092:18:18:89:539:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It follows that at least in this case, inflation and output determination can be understood
31:1127:81183:18:18:72:539:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:in exactly the same way as in the basic NK model,regardless of the average size of credit
31:1128:81272:18:18:72:540:111:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:frictions, or their degree of variability.For example, in the case that the monetary policy
31:1129:81363:18:18:72:540:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equation  involves  no  response  to  lagged  variables  (or  to  any  endogenous  variables  other
31:1130:81462:18:0:72:540:75:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than inflation, output, or forecasts of these), and the policy implies a determinate rational-
32:1131:81602:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expectations  equilibrium,  that  equilibrium  will  make  inflation,  output  and  interest  rates
32:1132:81701:18:15:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all a function solely of the economy’scurrent state— to be precise, the current values of
32:1133:81790:15:21:73:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ˆYnt,gt,ut,ˆωt,ˆΞt,and the monetary policy disturbance, and current information about the
32:1134:81879:21:18:71:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expected future evolution of these variables.  (As has often been remarked of the basic NK
32:1135:81969:18:18:71:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model, the model is thus “purely forward-looking,” and cannot explain inflation persistence
32:1136:82060:18:18:71:533:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other than as a consequence of persistence in the exogenous disturbances just mentioned.)
32:1137:82149:18:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the simple case of a monetary policy described by (3.13), the conditions for determinacy
32:1138:82240:18:18:71:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f14:B:of equilibrium remain exactly the same as in the basic NK model; in the case thatφπ,φy≥
32:1139:82327:18:18:71:539:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:0,these  amount  simply  to  the  requirement  that  the  policy  rule  conform  to  the  “Taylor
32:1140:82424:18:35:71:471:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Principle” (Woodford,2003, p.  254),i.e.,that the response coefficients satisfy
32:1141:82503:35:0:259:283:490:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:A:φπ+
32:1142:82506:0:16:287:314:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:?:1−β
32:1143:82509:16:0:297:304:482:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:?:κ
32:1144:82510:0:33:316:352:490:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:?:φy>1.
32:1145:82515:33:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:If this condition is satisfied, one can solve for inflation as a function of current and expected
32:1146:82612:18:18:72:540:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:future values of the disturbance processes in exactly the same way as is explained in Woodford
32:1147:82706:18:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2003, chap.  4, secs.  2.2, 2.4), and the coefficients on current and expected future values
32:1148:82799:18:17:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the disturbances  ̄ct,ˆGt, ̄ht,at,ˆμwt,ˆτt,or-mtat all horizons areidenticalto the predictions
32:1149:82896:17:18:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  basic  NK  model,  if  the  latter  model  is  calibrated  to  have  the  same  values  for  the
32:1150:83001:18:18:72:539:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:coefficientsβ,ξ, ̄σ,andωy.38The only difference in the solution is that shocks to the current
32:1151:83094:18:18:72:539:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or  expected  future  values  of  the  financial  disturbances  ˆωtandˆΞtwill  affect  equilibrium
32:1152:83192:18:18:72:156:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation as well.
32:1153:83210:18:18:89:539:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Moreover, not only does the model predict the same numerical responses to non-financial
32:1154:83297:18:18:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances, under given monetary-policy coefficients (φπ,φy) — so that one’s conclusions
32:1155:83387:18:18:72:540:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about the desirability of a particular choice of those coefficients, from the point of view of how
32:1156:83485:18:18:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they effect the economy’s response to non-financial disturbances, will be unchanged — but
32:1157:83574:18:18:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the predicted responses to financial disturbances do not really involve any new considerations
32:1158:83668:18:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(beyond the mere fact that such disturbances can occur and ought to be measured in order
32:1159:83756:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to properly conduct policy).  The effects of variations in the processes{ˆωt,ˆΞt}on inflation
32:1160:83849:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and output are predicted to be the same as the effects thatotherkinds of disturbances have,
32:1161:83940:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when they shift the three equations to a similar extent and with a similar expected degree of
32:1162:84033:18:17:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:persistence.  Thus the effects of financial shocks on inflation can be decomposed into three
32:1163:84125:17:16:81:539:135:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:38Of course, the numerical values of some of these coefficients may be different, owing to the existence of
32:1164:84232:16:12:72:540:119:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:credit frictions, than they would be in an economy without such frictions, owing, for example, to an effect
32:1165:84339:12:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of steady-state distortions resulting from credit spreads on the steady-state level of output, and hence the
32:1166:84447:12:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:point at which various elasticities are evaluated.  This would not, however, affect the accuracy of predictions
32:1167:84558:12:12:72:540:83:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:made by the NK model if it were correctly parameterized to match the elasticities observed in an actual
32:1168:84661:12:0:72:112:71:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:economy.
33:1169:84715:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:types of effects that are already present in the basic NK model:  the effects of a disturbance
33:1170:84809:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  the  “natural  rate  of  interest”  (a  shift  in  the  real  average  interest  rate  consistent  with
33:1171:84916:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  zero  output  gap),  the  effects  of  a  “cost-push  shock”  (a  shift  in  the  size  of  output  gap
33:1172:85022:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:required for price stability), and the effects of a “monetary policy shock” (a change in the
33:1173:85114:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average interest rate relative to what would ordinarily follow from the current inflation rate
33:1174:85208:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and output gap, in this case due to a change in the credit spread rather than a change in
33:1175:85297:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the policy rate).  Financial disturbances typically have effects of all three types;  but their
33:1176:85392:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consequences can be easily understood if the consequences of those three general types of
33:1177:85481:18:18:72:261:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances are already understood.
33:1178:85517:18:18:89:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The case in which{ˆωt,ˆΞt}are both completely exogenous processes is, of course, a fairly
33:1179:85606:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:special one.  If one or both of them depends on the volume of bank lending, as allowed for in
33:1180:85699:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our exposition above, a larger system of equations, including the law of motion for private
33:1181:85790:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:debt, is needed in order to predict the evolution of inflation, output and interest rates.  We
33:1182:85884:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do not seek to present analytical results for this more complex case, but instead offer some
33:1183:85976:18:39:72:221:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:illustrative numerical results.
33:1184:86007:39:26:72:238:397:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.2    Model Calibration
33:1185:86031:26:18:72:540:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The numerical values for parameters that are used in our calculations are explained in the
33:1186:86121:18:18:72:540:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Appendix.  Many of the model’s parameters are also parameters of the basic NK model, and
33:1187:86209:18:18:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the case of these parameters we assume similar numerical values as in the numerical anal-
33:1188:86301:18:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ysis of the basic NK model inWoodford(2003).  The new parameters that are also needed
33:1189:86386:18:18:71:539:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the present model are those relating to heterogeneity or to the specification of the credit
33:1190:86481:18:18:71:540:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frictions.  The parameters relating to heterogeneity are the fractionπbof households that
33:1191:86570:18:18:71:539:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are borrowers, the degree of persistenceδof a household’s “type”, the steady-state expendi-
33:1192:86661:18:17:71:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ture level of borrowers relative to savers,sb/ss, and the interest-elasticity of expenditure of
33:1193:86756:17:18:71:296:228:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers relative to that of savers,σb/σs.39
33:1194:86801:18:18:89:540:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the calculations reported here,  we assume thatπb=πs= 0.5,so that there are an
33:1195:86882:18:18:71:539:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equal  number  of  borrowers  and  savers.   We  assume  thatδ=  0.975,so  that  the  expected
33:1196:86976:18:18:71:539:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time until a household has access to the insurance agency (and its type is drawn again) is 10
33:1197:87069:18:18:71:539:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:years.  This means that the expected path of the spread between lending and deposit rates
33:1198:87158:18:18:71:539:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for 10 years or so into the future affects current spending decisions, but that expectations
33:1199:87250:18:16:81:539:120:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:39Another new parameter as a consequence of heterogeneity is the steady-state level of government debt
33:1200:87352:16:11:72:539:104:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:relative to GDP, ̄bg/ ̄Y .This parameter need not be specified in the representative-household basic NK model,
33:1201:87462:11:12:72:540:93:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:since changes in it simply imply a different steady-state level of net transfers, and the size of these does not
33:1202:87574:12:12:72:540:81:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:affect any of the equilibrium relations.  In the model with heterogeneity, it does matter, because of the failure
33:1203:87687:12:0:72:486:69:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f15:F:of Ricardian equivalence noted above.  But in our baseline calculations, we assume that ̄bg= 0.
34:1204:87828:0:18:72:438:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regarding the spread several decades in the future are nearly irrelevant.
34:1205:87901:18:18:89:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We calibrate the degree of heterogeneity in the steady-state expenditure shares of the two
34:1206:87991:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:types so that the implied steady-state debt ̄bis equal to 80 percent of annual steady-state
34:1207:88082:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:output.40This value matches the median ratio of private (non-financial,  non-government,
34:1208:88170:18:18:72:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:B:non-mortgage) debt to GDP over the period 1986-2008.41This requires a ratiosb/ss= 1.27.
34:1209:88257:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  calibrate  the  value  ofσb/σsto  equal  5.   This  is  an  arbitrary  choice,  though  the  fact
34:1210:88358:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  borrowers  are  assumed  to  have  a  greater  willingness  to  substitute  intertemporally  is
34:1211:88459:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:important, as this results in the prediction that an exogenous tightening of monetary policy
34:1212:88551:18:18:72:539:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(a positive value of the residual-mtin (3.13)) results in a reduction in the equilibrium volume
34:1213:88646:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of creditbt(see Figures 2 and 5 below).  This is consistent with VAR evidence on the effects
34:1214:88738:18:18:72:405:507:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of an identified monetary policy shock on household borrowing.42
34:1215:88802:18:18:89:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It  is  also  necessary  to  specify  the  steady-state  values  of  the  functionsω(b)  and  Ξ(b)
34:1216:88900:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  describe  the  financial  frictions,  in  addition  to  making  clear  what  kinds  of  random
34:1217:89000:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perturbations of these functions we wish to consider when analyzing the effects of “financial
34:1218:89093:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shocks.”  We here mainly present results for two cases.  In each case, we assume that there is
34:1219:89187:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no steady-state default risk (  ̄χ(b) = 0), so that the steady-state credit spread is due entirely
34:1220:89285:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the marginal resource cost of intermediation.  But we do allow for exogenous shocks to
34:1221:89374:18:33:72:500:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the default rate (which then becomes slightly positive); specifically, we assume that
34:1222:89459:33:33:275:336:349:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:A:χt(b) =  ̃χtb,
34:1223:89473:33:18:72:539:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where{ ̃χt}is an exogenous disturbance process taking non-negative values.  The “financial
34:1224:89563:18:18:71:373:298:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:shock” in Figure 15below is an exogenous increase in   ̃χt.43
34:1225:89624:18:18:89:539:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We consider two cases that differ in the specification of the (time-invariant) intermedi-
34:1226:89713:18:17:71:540:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ation  technology  Ξ(b).In  the  case  of  alinear  intermediation  technology(not  shown),  we
34:1227:89808:17:18:71:539:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suppose that Ξ(b) =  ̄ωb,while in the case of aconvex intermediation technology(shown in

34:1230:89938:19:12:81:313:190:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f15:A:40In our quarterly model, this means that ̄b/ ̄Y= 3.2.
34:1231:89992:12:15:81:539:178:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:41We  exclude  mortgage  debt  when  calibrating  the  degree  of  heterogeneity  of  preferences  in  our  model,
34:1232:90106:15:12:72:540:163:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:since mortgage debt is incurred in order to acquire an asset, rather than to consume current produced goods
34:1233:90213:12:9:72:193:151:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in excess of current income.
34:1234:90241:9:12:81:352:142:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:42See, for example,Den Haan, Sumner and Yamashiro(2010).
34:1235:90297:12:15:81:539:130:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:43In treating the “financial shock” as involving an increase in markups but no increase in the real resources
34:1236:90406:15:12:72:540:115:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:used in banking, we followGerali, Neri and Signoretti(2008).  These authors cite the Eurosystem’s quarterly
34:1237:90513:12:12:72:540:103:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Bank Lending Survey as showing that since October 2007, banks in the euro area had “strongly increased
34:1238:90615:12:0:72:327:91:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the margins charged on average and riskier loans” (p.  24).
35:1239:90720:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  someη >1.44In  both  cases,  in  our  numerical  analyses  we  assume  a  steady-state
35:1240:90811:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit  spread   ̄ωequal  to  2.0  percentage  points  per  annum,45following  Mehra,  Piguillem
35:1241:90907:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Prescott  (2008).46(Combined  with  our  assumption  that  “types”  persist  for  10  years
35:1242:91003:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on  average,  this  implies  a  steady-state  “marginal  utility  gap” ̄Ω≡ ̄λb/ ̄λs=  1.22,so  that
35:1243:91102:18:18:71:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there would be a non-trivial welfare gain from transferring further resources from savers to
35:1244:91194:18:18:71:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:borrowers.)  In the case of the convex technology,  we setηso that a one-percent increase
35:1245:91283:18:18:71:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:in the volume of credit increases the credit spread by one percentage point (per annum).47
35:1246:91373:18:18:71:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The assumption thatη >1 allows our model to match the prediction of VAR estimates that
35:1247:91459:18:18:71:539:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an unexpected tightening of monetary policy is associated with a slight reduction in credit
35:1248:91550:18:18:71:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads (see,e.g.,Lown and Morgan,2002).  We have chosen a rather extreme value for this
35:1249:91638:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:elasticity in our calibration of the convex-technology case, in order to make more visible the
35:1250:91732:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference that a convex technology makes for our results.  (In the case of a smaller value of
35:1251:91826:18:17:71:540:471:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:η,the results for the convex technology are closer to those for the linear technology, and in
35:1252:91919:17:18:71:539:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fact are in many respects similar to those for an economy with no financial frictions at all.)
35:1253:92013:18:18:89:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As a first exercise, we consider the implied equilibrium responses of the model’s endoge-
35:1254:92102:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nous variables to the various kinds of exogenous disturbances,  under the assumption that
35:1255:92191:18:18:71:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy is described by a Taylor rule of the form (3.13).  The coefficients of the mon-
35:1256:92286:18:18:71:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:etary policy rule are assigned the valuesφπ= 2 andφy= 0.25 as in Woodford (2003, chap.
35:1257:92372:18:18:71:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:4), allowing comparison between our quantitative results here and those presented there for
35:1258:92463:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  calibrated  representative-household  model.   Among  other  disturbances,  we  consider  the
35:1259:92559:18:18:71:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects of random disturbances to the error term-mtin the monetary policy rule.  Later, we
35:1260:92649:18:18:71:401:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consider the predicted dynamics under optimal monetary policy.
