35:1279:94142:9:0:81:211:122:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f15:A:47This requires thatη= 51.6.
36:1280:94216:0:26:72:239:687:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.3    Numerical Results
36:1281:94240:26:18:72:540:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We begin by considering the predicted responses to aggregate disturbances of a kind that
36:1282:94328:18:18:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also exist in the basic NK model, in order to determine how accurate that model’s answers
36:1283:94417:18:18:72:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  about  the  questions  to  which  itgivesanswers.   We  first  consider  the  case  of  a  linear
36:1284:94519:18:18:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediation technology.  In this case, the credit spreadωtevolves exogenously, as assumed
36:1285:94611:18:18:72:540:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the discussion at the end of section 1.1, but Ξtis no longer independent ofbt.  Nonetheless,
36:1286:94706:18:18:72:540:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in this  case we continue to find  that  for a  reasonable  parameterization  of the quantity of
36:1287:94802:18:18:72:540:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:resources used in intermediation, the existence of credit frictions makes virtually no difference
36:1288:94899:18:18:72:326:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the predicted equilibrium responses to shocks.
36:1289:94949:18:17:89:540:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This is illustrated in Figures2-4for three particular types of exogenous disturbances.  In
36:1290:95039:17:18:72:540:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure2 we consider the equilibrium responses to a contractionary monetary policy shock,
36:1291:95127:18:18:72:539:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:represented  by  a  unit  (one  percentage  point,  annualized)  increase  in-mt.We  furthermore
36:1292:95223:18:18:72:540:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assume  that  the  policy  disturbance  is  persistent;  specifically,-mtis  assumed  to  follow  an
36:1293:95323:18:18:72:540:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:AR(1) process with coefficient of autocorrelationρ= 0.75.The separate panels of the figure
36:1294:95413:18:18:72:539:428:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:indicate the impulse responses of output, inflation,48the deposit rate, the lending rate,49
36:1295:95504:18:18:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and aggregate private debt respectively.  Figure3 illustrates the equilibrium responses of the
36:1296:95598:18:18:72:540:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:same variables to a unit positive innovation in the productivity factor, where the disturbance
36:1297:95692:18:18:72:540:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is again assumed to have an autocorrelation of 0.75, and monetary policy is conducted in
36:1298:95780:18:18:72:539:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accordance with (3.13) with no random term.  Figure4 shows the corresponding equilibrium
36:1299:95868:18:18:72:540:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responses in response to an increase in government purchases by an amount equal to one
36:1300:95954:18:18:72:193:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percent of total output.
36:1301:95978:18:18:89:539:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In each figure, the predicted impulse responses under our model with financial frictions
36:1302:96066:18:17:72:540:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(the case labeled ‘FF’ in each figure) are contrasted with those under two variant parameter-
36:1303:96159:17:18:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:izations of the model.  The case labeled ‘NoFF’ corresponds to an otherwise identical model
36:1304:96250:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in whichωt(b)≡0 and Ξt(b)≡0, but we retain the heterogeneity in preferences, parame-
36:1305:96334:18:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terized in the same way as in the ‘FF’ model.  The case labeled ‘RepHH’ is one in which in
36:1306:96424:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:addition to assuming zero credit frictions, we assume identical preferences for the two types;
36:1307:96518:18:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this model is equivalent to a representative-household model (specifically, to the basic NK
36:1308:96609:18:19:72:539:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model as presented inWoodford,2003, chap.  4).  Comparison of these three cases allows us
36:1309:96698:19:15:81:539:158:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:48In the plots, both the inflation rate and the interest rates are reported as annualized rates, so that 0.10
36:1310:96807:15:12:72:540:143:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:means an increase in the inflation rate of 10 basis points per annum.  In terms of our quarterly model, what
36:1311:96915:12:8:72:362:131:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f15:F:is plotted is not the response ofπt, but rather the response of 4πt.
36:1312:96983:8:16:81:539:123:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:49In the present model, the spread between the deposit rate and the lending rate is exogenously fixed, and
36:1313:97089:16:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:so these two variables necessarily respond by exactly the same amount, except in the case of a shock to the
36:1314:97196:12:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:exogenous credit spread itself.  However, we include both panels as we use the same format for the figures
36:1315:97302:12:0:72:319:83:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:to follow, when inclusion of both is no longer redundant.
37:1316:97405:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to separately consider the degree to which credit frictions as opposed to heterogeneity make
37:1317:97497:18:18:72:133:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a difference.
37:1318:97510:18:18:89:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In each of Figures2 through4, we observe that the impulse responses of output, inflation,
37:1319:97599:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  the  two  interest  rates  are  virtually  identical  under  all  three  parameterizations  of  the
37:1320:97703:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model.   (The  same  is  true  for  the  other  aggregate  disturbances  that  have  analogs  in  the
37:1321:97804:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:representative-household model — a common disturbance to the impatience to consume of
37:1322:97889:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all households, a disturbance to the disutility of work, a shock to government purchases, a
37:1323:97980:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shock to the tax rate,  or a shock to the wage markup — though we do not include these
37:1324:98066:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:figures here.)  We have already explained in section 2.1 why this would be true in the case
37:1325:98157:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  the  resources  used  in  intermediation  are  independent  of  the  volume  of  lending.   Our
37:1326:98258:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:numerical  results  indicate  that  even  when  we  assume  that  intermediation  uses  resources
37:1327:98355:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(and  indeed  that  credit  spreads  are  entirely  due  to  the  marginal  resource  cost  of  making
37:1328:98457:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:additional loans), and that the required resources are proportional to the volume of lending,
37:1329:98550:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneity and the existence of a steady-state credit spread (of a realistic magnitude) still
37:1330:98646:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:make only a negligible difference.  This is because the contribution of the banking sector to
37:1331:98739:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the overall variation in the aggregate demand for produced goods and services is still quite
37:1332:98831:18:18:72:109:400:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:small.50
37:1333:98839:18:18:89:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Financial frictions matter somewhat more for equilibrium dynamics if we also assume that
37:1334:98927:18:18:72:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit spreads vary endogenously with the volume of lending.  Figures5-9show equilibrium
37:1335:99015:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responses of the same aggregate variables to a variety of types of exogenous disturbances, in
37:1336:99108:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the case of the “convex intermediation technology” calibration discussed in section 2.2.  Fig-
37:1337:99202:18:18:72:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ures5-7show responses to the same three kinds of shocks as in Figures2-4respectively, but
37:1338:99291:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the alternative intermediation technology.  Figure8 shows the corresponding responses to
37:1339:99383:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an exogenous increase in the impatience to consume of savers; and Figure9 shows responses
37:1340:99472:18:18:72:540:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to an exogenous increase in real government debt by an amount equal to 1 percent of GDP.
37:1341:99560:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In each case, the disturbance is modeled as an AR(1) process with autoregressive coefficient
37:1342:99652:18:17:72:96:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:0.75.
37:1343:99657:17:18:89:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the case of the monetary policy shock (Figure5), we again find that the equilibrium
37:1344:99743:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responses of output and inflation are nearly the same in all three models, though the ‘FF
37:1345:99832:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model’ is no longer quite so indistinguishable from the ‘NoFF’ model.  The most important
37:1346:99921:18:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of allowing for endogeneity of the credit spread is on the implied responses of interest
37:1347:100016:18:19:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates to the shock. Because credit contracts in response to this shock (as noted earlier, though
37:1348:100112:19:15:81:540:112:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:50Note that in each of Figures2-4, the existence of the credit frictions in the ‘FF’ model makes a substantial
37:1349:100222:15:12:72:539:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:difference for the equilibrium evolution of creditbtrelative to the prediction of the ‘NoFF’ model.  However,
37:1350:100331:12:12:72:540:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:this change in the size of the banking sector does not have substantial consequences for aggregate output,
37:1351:100437:12:0:72:235:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:employment, or inflationary pressure.
38:1352:100520:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:now  by  less  than  in  Figure  2),  the  spread  between  the  lending  rate  and  the  deposit  rate
38:1353:100623:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decreases, in accordance with the empirical finding ofLown and Morgan(2002).  This means
38:1354:100711:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the deposit rate need no longer decline as much as does the lending rate.  Moreover,
38:1355:100800:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because the reduced spread has an expansionary effect on aggregate demand, output declines
38:1356:100890:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:slightly less in response to the shock than in the ‘NoFF’ model; this is also a reason for the
38:1357:100984:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deposit rate to decline less.  Thus the most visible effect is on the predicted response of the
38:1358:101079:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deposit rate, which is visibly smaller in the ‘FF model.’  The effects of financial frictions are
38:1359:101176:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similarly mainly on the path of the deposit rate in the case of a shock to the sales tax rate
38:1360:101269:18:18:72:149:543:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:τt(not shown).
38:1361:101283:18:18:89:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The effects of financial frictions are not quite as trivial in the case of the technology shock
38:1362:101378:18:18:72:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Figure6).  Though again the largest effect is on the path of the deposit rate, in this case the
38:1363:101474:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endogeneity of the credit spread also has non-negligible effects on the equilibrium response
38:1364:101566:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of output.  (The primary reason for the difference is that this shock has a larger immediate
38:1365:101658:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect on the path of credit, and hence a larger immediate effect on the equilibrium spread in
38:1366:101752:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the case of the convex technology.)  Because an increase in productivity leads to an expansion
38:1367:101846:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of credit, credit spreads now increase in the ‘FF model’; this is has a contractionary effect on
38:1368:101942:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate demand, so that output increases less than in the ‘NoFF model’.  Similar effects of
38:1369:102035:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial frictions are observed in the case of a disturbance to the disutility of working (an
38:1370:102129:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exogenous increase in the multiplicative factor ̄Htin (2.23)).  The effects of an increase in
38:1371:102222:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the wage markupμwtor the tax rateτtare likewise similar, but with opposite signs to the
38:1372:102309:18:18:71:202:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects shown in Figure6.
38:1373:102334:18:18:89:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The effects of financial frictions are even more significant in the case of a shock to gov-
38:1374:102425:18:18:71:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ernment purchases (Figure7) or to the consumption demand of savers (Figure8).51These
38:1375:102509:18:18:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  both  disturbances  that  crowd  out  the  expenditure  of  private  borrowers  (as  the  most
38:1376:102608:18:18:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest-sensitive  category  of  expenditure)  to  a  significant  extent,  and  so  substantially  re-
38:1377:102712:18:18:71:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duce equilibrium borrowing and credit spreads.  In each case, the reduction in spreads has a
38:1378:102804:18:17:71:539:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:further expansionary effect on aggregate demand, so that output increases by more than in
38:1379:102893:17:18:71:166:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the ‘NoFF’ model.
38:1380:102910:18:18:89:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Note that the effect would be quite different in the case of a shock to the consumption
38:1381:102997:18:18:71:539:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand  ofborrowersrather  than  savers  (not  shown).   In  this  case,  private  credit  would
38:1382:103093:18:18:71:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase rather than decreasing, and by less than in Figure8, because of the greater interest-
38:1383:103187:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:elasticity of the demand of borrowers; this would imply a small increase in spreads, making
38:1384:103278:18:18:71:539:113:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:the disturbance slightly less expansionary, but with a less dramatic effect than in Figure8.52
38:1385:103372:18:12:81:518:95:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:51The shock considered here increases the value ofcs(λ) by one percent for each possible value ofλ.
38:1386:103471:12:0:81:539:83:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:52The effect of financial frictions in this case is somewhat similar to the case of the technology shock shown
39:1387:103627:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The aggregate effects of financial frictions are even smaller in the case of a uniform increase

39:1390:103896:18:18:89:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally,  the consequences of financial frictions are of particular qualitative significance
39:1391:103988:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the case of a disturbance to the path of government debt (Figure 9).  Here we consider a
39:1392:104079:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbance to fiscal policy that temporarily increases the level of government debt, through
39:1393:104172:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a lump-sum transfer to households, which is then gradually taken back over a period of time,
39:1394:104264:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so that the path of real government debt is eventually the same as it would have been in

39:1396:104450:18:18:72:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:as  in  the  representative  household  model;  and  so  in  these  cases,  the  fiscal  shock  hasno
39:1397:104551:18:18:72:539:507:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:effecton output, inflation, or interest rates.  However, an increase in government borrowing

39:1399:104733:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduced private borrowing implies a reduction in spreads.  This has an expansionary effect on
39:1400:104826:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate demand, with the consequence that both output and inflation increase, as shown
39:1401:104914:18:18:72:145:436:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:in the figure.53
39:1402:104930:18:18:89:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To sum up, we find that under an empirically realistic calibration of the average size of
39:1403:105019:18:18:72:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit spreads, the mere existence of a positive credit spread doesnotimply any substantial

39:1409:105578:18:18:71:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cially in the case of types of disturbances — such as variations in government borrowing, or

41:1485:109427:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for optimality admit astationary(or steady state) solution, in which the rate of inflation is
41:1486:109520:18:18:72:539:597:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:zero.  Hence under an optimal policy commitment, in the absence of stochastic disturbances
41:1487:109610:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the inflation rate will eventually converge to zero;55and in the case of small enough stochastic
41:1488:109706:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances, the optimal policy commitment will involve an inflation rate that fluctuates
41:1489:109796:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asymptotically  around  zero.   To  the  extent  that  the  disturbances  are  small  enough  for  a
41:1490:109896:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:linear approximation to the equilibrium relations to provide an adequate approximation to
41:1491:109985:18:18:72:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the equilibrium dynamics, optimal policy involves along-run averageinflation rate of zero,
41:1492:110075:18:18:72:211:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:even in the stochastic case.
41:1493:110103:18:17:89:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This result generalizes the one obtained byBenigno and Woodford(2005) for the case with
41:1494:110190:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:representative-household, and implies that the optimal inflation target is independent of the
41:1495:110283:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(average) severity of the distortions resulting from credit frictions, just as it is independent
41:1496:110379:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  severity  of  the  steady-state  distortions  resulting  from  market  power  in  the  goods
41:1497:110480:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or labor markets or from distorting taxes.  This indicates a first important respect in which
41:1498:110573:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conclusions about optimal policy derived from a model that abstracts from financial frictions
41:1499:110666:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:continue to apply when one allows for such frictions.  The result also justifies our attention
41:1500:110760:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:here only to the consequences of alternative policies that imply a long-run average inflation
41:1501:110853:18:18:72:539:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate near zero (as in our analysis of the consequences of a Taylor rule in section2);  since
41:1502:110945:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we  know  that  the  optimal  policy  commitment  involves  inflation  fluctuations  around  zero,
41:1503:111043:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we  can  restrict  our  analysis  to  policies  with  that  property,  both  when  seeking  to  further
41:1504:111146:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characterize  optimal  policy,  and  when  investigating  the  desirability  of  simple  policy  rules
41:1505:111248:18:18:72:322:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that are intended to approximate optimal policy.
41:1506:111296:18:15:81:539:238:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:55Under a once-and-for-all commitment chosen to maximize the objective (4.1) at some initial date, under
41:1507:111400:15:12:72:540:223:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:no  constraints  other  than  those  required  for  a  perfect  foresight  equilibrium  from  the  time  of  adoption  of
41:1508:111521:12:12:72:540:211:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the policy commitment onward — the “Ramsey” policy problem — a higher inflation rate will be chosen
41:1509:111620:12:12:72:540:199:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:initially, in order to exploit the short-run aggregate-supply trade-off without having to take account of any
41:1510:111729:12:12:72:540:187:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:consequences of anticipation of such inflation in the period prior to adoption of the policy; but the policy will
41:1511:111842:12:12:72:540:175:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:involve a commitment to eventually reduce the inflation rate to zero, since the long-run inflation commitment
41:1512:111951:12:12:72:539:163:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:internalizes the consequences of anticipation of the inflation rate in prior periods.  (See Woodford,2003, chap.
41:1513:112063:12:12:72:540:151:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:7, for discussion of this in the context of the basic NK model.)  Optimal policy “from a timeless perspective,”
41:1514:112174:12:12:72:540:139:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in the sense defined inWoodford(2003, chapter 7) andBenigno and Woodford(2005), instead involves zero
41:1515:112275:12:0:71:346:127:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:inflation at all times, in the absence of stochastic disturbances.
42:1516:112387:0:26:72:294:687:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Linear-Quadratic Analysis
42:1517:112419:26:18:72:540:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Under certain simplifying assumptions, we can obtain an analytical solution for the optimal
42:1518:112510:18:18:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state-contingent policy — or more precisely,  for a linear approximation to optimal policy,
42:1519:112601:18:18:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the case of small enough fluctuations around the optimal (zero-inflation) long-run steady
42:1520:112693:18:18:72:539:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state — using the method of linear-quadratic approximation introduced inRotemberg and
42:1521:112778:18:18:72:540:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Woodford(1997) and further expounded byBenigno and Woodford(2012).56Under these
42:1522:112857:18:18:72:540:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions, we can derive a quadratic loss function for monetary stabilization policy with
42:1523:112948:18:18:72:540:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the property that minimization of the loss function is equivalent (in the case of small enough
42:1524:113042:18:18:72:540:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances)  to  maximization  of  the  utility-based  objective  (4.1).   The  linear  policy  rule
42:1525:113144:18:17:72:540:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  minimizes  the  quadratic  loss  function  subject  to  the  linear  constraints  obtained  by
42:1526:113244:17:18:72:540:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:log-linearizing the model structural relations (as in section 2.1) then provides a linear ap-
42:1527:113337:18:18:72:228:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proximation to optimal policy.
42:1528:113367:18:18:89:539:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We begin by using structural relation (2.15) together with the definition Ωt≡λbt/λstto
42:1529:113453:18:18:71:539:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:solve forλbtandλstas functions ofYt,Ωt,Ξt,and the exogenous disturbances.  Substituting
42:1530:113540:18:18:71:539:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these solutions into (4.2), we obtain a period utility function ̃U(Yt,Ωt,Ξt,∆t; ̃ξt) to replace
42:1531:113635:18:18:71:539:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the functionUdefined in (4.2).  We then compute a quadratic (Taylor-series) approximation
42:1532:113724:18:18:71:540:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  the  function ̃Uaround  the  values  of  its  arguments  in  the  zero-inflation  steady  state,
42:1533:113824:18:18:71:540:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:( ̄Y , ̄Ω, ̄Ξ,1; 0).This takes an especially simple form under the following special assumptions:
42:1534:113921:18:18:71:540:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(i)  the  steady-state  tax  distortion   ̄τexactly  cancels  the  distortion  resulting  from  market
42:1535:114023:18:18:71:540:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:power in the goods markets (1−τ=μp≡θ/(θ−1)), so that in the zero-inflation steady
42:1536:114104:18:18:71:539:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state, price is equal to marginal cost; (ii) there is no steady-state wage markup ( ̄μw= 1); (iii)
42:1537:114202:18:18:71:539:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the steady-state credit spread  ̄ω= 0 (which, because of relation (3.4), implies that ̄Ω = 1 as
42:1538:114297:18:17:71:539:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well); and (iv) there are no resources consumed by the intermediary sector in steady state
42:1539:114387:17:18:71:540:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:( ̄Ξ = 0).  Note that the assumed absence ofsteady-statedistortions of any of these kinds does
42:1540:114481:18:18:71:539:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not mean that we cannot consider the effects of these distortions; as with the other exogenous
42:1541:114575:18:18:71:539:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disturbances, we consider the effects of small departures from the steady-state values.  But
42:1542:114667:18:18:71:539:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the special case considered in this section, each of these distortions is assumed to be of
42:1543:114760:18:18:71:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:orderO(||ξ||) in the notation ofWoodford(2003, chap.  6).  Finally, we also assume (v) that
42:1544:114851:18:18:71:539:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the gradient ̄Ξb= 0 in steady state as well, so that anyendogenousvariation in the resources
42:1545:114943:18:18:71:539:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used by the banking sector is of at most second order, though we allow for variations in the
42:1546:115035:18:15:81:539:141:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:56These simplifying assumptions are not required in order to compute a valid LQ approximation to our
42:1547:115135:15:12:72:539:126:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:policy problem, as explained inBenigno and Woodford(2012).  However, in general, the algebraic expression
42:1548:115240:12:12:72:540:114:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of the solution to the LQ problem will be complex, so we discuss it here only in a special case allowing a
42:1549:115346:12:12:72:540:102:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:solution of a simple form.  The same general method is used, however, to approximately characterize optimal

44:1612:119322:18:17:72:148:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimal policy.

45:1643:122103:37:0:253:266:470:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f4:?:E0

45:1648:122221:17:18:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of stabilization policy remain as in the basic NK model; the only differences made by financial

45:1651:122491:18:18:89:539:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Time-variation  in  financial  frictions  does  matter  for  the  optimal  conduct  of  monetary

45:1653:122683:18:18:72:540:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:However, only the latter relation represents a constraint upon the set of achievable outcomes
45:1654:122776:18:18:72:540:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the target variables, inflation and the output gap. And the only effect of financial frictions
45:1655:122874:18:18:72:540:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on this relation is the presence of an additional additive disturbance term.  The first-order

45:1660:123363:18:18:72:540:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditions for optimality to be satisfied.  Just as in the basic NK model, the optimal target
45:1661:123456:18:17:72:195:176:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:criterion is of the form61
45:1662:123482:17:19:237:539:159:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:A:πt+ (λy/κ)(xt−xt−1) = 0.(4.8)
45:1663:123511:19:16:81:540:140:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:60For example, we may assume that (i) no real resources are used in intermediation, so that Ξt(b) = 0,

46:1668:124029:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:While the state-contingent paths for inflation and the output gap thatsatisfythis criterion

46:1672:124402:18:39:72:536:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:target criterion is of an identical form to what is optimal in the absence of credit frictions.
46:1673:124497:39:26:72:346:576:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.2    Implementing the Optimal Policy
46:1674:124535:26:18:72:540:550:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The implementation of an optimal policy does require the central bank to monitor the varying
46:1675:124627:18:18:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:size of the credit frictions — more precisely, the varying size of credit spreads — in order to
46:1676:124722:18:18:72:540:514:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determine how it must act in order to ensure fulfillment of the target criterion (4.8).  These
46:1677:124816:18:17:72:540:496:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matter for two reasons.  First, the paths of inflation and the output gap consistent with (4.8)
46:1678:124911:17:18:72:540:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depend in general on the evolution of credit spreads, because of the effect of those spreads
46:1679:125003:18:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the aggregate-supply trade-off (3.12).  And second, the path of policy rates required to
46:1680:125094:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implement  given  (feasible)  paths  for  inflation  and  output  depends  on  the  path  of  credit
46:1681:125194:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads,  because  of  their  effects  on  both  the  relation  (3.8)  between  average  interest  rates
46:1682:125298:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and expenditure and the relation (3.10) between the policy rate and the relevant “average”
46:1683:125388:18:18:72:137:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rate.
46:1684:125402:18:18:89:539:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The required adjustment of the policy rate follows from standard treatments (e.g.,Clar-

46:1686:125579:18:18:71:539:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to “cost-push shocks” and variations in the natural rate of interest in the context of the basic

47:1707:127224:18:18:89:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A useful description of the ultimate implications for interest-rate policy can be given by
47:1708:127314:18:18:71:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:solving equilibrium relations (3.8), (3.10) and (3.12) for the policy rate required in order for
47:1709:127410:18:18:71:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the equilibrium values ofπtandxtto satisfy the target criterion (4.8).  In this exercise we

47:1711:127590:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predetermined or exogenous variables; solve for the implied values ofπtandxtconditional
47:1712:127677:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:upon the choice ofidt; substitute these solutions forπtandxtinto the target criterion; and
47:1713:127767:18:17:71:539:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then  solve  for  the  value  ofidtthat  implies  that  (4.8)  should  be  satisfied.   The  resulting
47:1714:127869:17:18:71:539:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest-rate reaction function is what Evans and Honkapohja (2006) call an “expectations-
47:1715:127959:18:18:71:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:based reaction function.”  Because it responds directly to (observed) current expectations,
47:1716:128050:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such a policy ensures that the target criterion is satisfiedregardlessof whether expectations
47:1717:128143:18:18:71:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are those consistent with the optimal equilibrium. Such an approach to the implementation of
47:1718:128235:18:18:71:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy has important advantages; in particular, it ensures both that the optimal equilibrium is
47:1719:128330:18:18:71:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the only (non-explosive) rational-expectations equilibrium consistent with the central bank’s
47:1720:128423:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reaction  function,  and  that  this  equilibrium  is  “E-stable,”  facilitating  convergence  to  the
47:1721:128525:18:18:71:451:328:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:rational-expectations equilibrium under least-squares learning dynamics.63
47:1722:128599:18:18:89:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the case of the model developed here (under the assumptions used to derive (4.8), this

47:1735:128877:30:18:72:540:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The terms on the first line of (4.9) are exactly the reaction function derived byEvans and
