48:1739:129268:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that must be added in the case of credit frictions, taking into account the effects of credit
48:1740:129361:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads and of the resources used in intermediation on the effective natural rate of interest,
48:1741:129455:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the cost-push effects of credit spreads, and the consequences of spreads for the gap between
48:1742:129547:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the policy rate and the average interest rate.  (We have written the terms on the second line
48:1743:129640:18:18:72:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in terms of  ˆωtandˆΩtrather thanˆΩtandEtˆΩt+1,by using (3.4) to eliminate the expected
48:1744:129727:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gap  term.   This  makes  it  easiest  to  contrast  the  effects  of  transitory  as  opposed  to  more
48:1745:129831:18:18:72:272:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:persistent variations in credit spreads.)
48:1746:129872:18:18:89:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Because the coefficient multiplying ˆωtis negative, while the term multiplyingˆΩtis positive
48:1747:129964:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(under the assumption thatsbσb> ssσs), the appropriate adjustment of the intercept of the
48:1748:130053:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reaction function is generally negative in the case of a transitory increase in credit spreads,
48:1749:130148:18:18:72:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:butless negative(for any given size of increase in credit spreads) the more persistent the
48:1750:130238:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase is expected to be.  It is furthermore worth noting that in the limiting case in which
48:1751:130332:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:sbσb>> ssσsandδapproaches  1,  the  coefficient  on  ˆωtin  (4.9)  approaches  -1.   Since  the
48:1752:130427:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:coefficient onˆΩtis also fairly small under a realistic calibration (about 0.03 in the calibration
48:1753:130525:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used above), it follows that the optimal reduction in the policy rate (relative to what the
48:1754:130616:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reaction  function  would  otherwise  call  for)  in  response  to  a  purely  transitory  increase  in
48:1755:130719:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit spreads will equal nearly 100 percent of the increase in spreads, as proposed by Taylor
48:1756:130813:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2008) and McCulley and Toloui (2008). In this limiting case, it is really only the interest rate
48:1757:130910:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:faced by borrowers that matters for aggregate demand, and thus it is only the consequence
48:1758:130999:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the policy rate for the rate that will be faced by borrowers that matters for fulfillment
48:1759:131091:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the target criterion;  in this case the reasoning of Taylor and of McCulley and Toloui is
48:1760:131183:18:18:72:166:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:essentially correct.
48:1761:131203:18:18:89:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Even in the case of a less extreme parameterization of the structural model and a more
48:1762:131289:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:persistent  disturbances  to  credit  markets,  the  optimal  adjustment  can  easily  be  a  large
48:1763:131388:18:18:72:540:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fraction of the size of the increase in credit spreads. For example, in the case of the calibration
48:1764:131487:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed above and in the case of a financial shock with the degree of persistence assumed in
48:1765:131581:18:17:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figures 15 below (i.e.,an autoregressive coefficient of 0.75), the reduction in the intercept of
48:1766:131677:17:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the central-bank reaction function will be by about 85 basis points for each percentage point
48:1767:131770:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase  in  credit  spreads.   However,  under  a  parameterization  in  which  the  expenditure
48:1768:131868:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decisions of borrowers are not so largely responsible for the interest sensitivity of aggregate
48:1769:131963:18:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expenditure,  the  optimal  reduction  in  the  policy  rate  in  response  to  an  increase  in  credit
48:1770:132067:18:18:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads would be smaller.  For example, in the case thatsbσb=ssσs, the coefficient on ˆωtis
48:1771:132158:18:18:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equal to exactly−πb,while the coefficient onˆΩtis zero.  In this case, it is only optimal to
48:1772:132250:18:18:72:539:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduce the policy rate byπbpercentage points for every percentage point increase in credit
48:1773:132340:18:0:72:540:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads; in this case, the optimal reaction function is most simply expressed in terms of an
49:1774:132478:0:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:operating target foriavgt, rather than eitheridtoribt.  (It is also interesting to note that in this
49:1775:132578:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case, the optimal response is independent of the degree of persistence of the disturbance to
49:1776:132670:18:18:72:153:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit markets.)
49:1777:132686:18:18:89:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:These  analytical  results  depend,  of  course,  on  a  number  of  simplifying  assumptions.
49:1778:132780:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Matters are more complicated, in particular, if we assume that either the resources used in
49:1779:132871:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial intermediation, the size of credit spreads, or both depend on the volume of bank
49:1780:132961:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lending.   Rather  than  seek  analytical  results  in  the  more  general  case,  we  present  some
49:1781:133061:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:illustrative numerical calculations of optimal policy in calibrated examples, and investigate
49:1782:133154:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the degree to which the insights suggested by the analysis of this simple case continue to
49:1783:133244:18:39:72:103:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:apply.
49:1784:133250:39:25:72:246:486:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.3    Numerical Analysis
49:1785:133275:25:18:72:540:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In order to check the degree to which the results obtained above for a special case continue to
49:1786:133370:18:18:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hold, at least approximately, under more general assumptions, we numerically analyze opti-
49:1787:133460:18:18:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mal policy in the calibrated economies for which we have already analyzed the consequences
49:1788:133550:18:18:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a simple Taylor rule in section 2.  Under assumptions more general than those used in
49:1789:133638:18:18:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the previous section, we can characterize the optimal responses to exogenous disturbances
49:1790:133727:18:18:72:540:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  various  sorts  by  deriving  the  first-order  conditions  that  characterize  optimal  (Ramsey)
49:1791:133828:18:18:72:540:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy — the problem of maximizing (4.1) subject to constraints (2.7)–(2.8), (2.12)–(2.15),
49:1792:133919:18:18:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2.26)–(2.27), and (2.28)–(2.29) — and then log-linearizing them around the zero-inflation
49:1793:134009:18:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimal steady state.  The resulting log-linear equations can be solved for log-linear optimal
49:1794:134103:18:18:72:540:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic responses of the various endogenous variables to (small enough) random shocks to
49:1795:134191:18:18:72:301:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each of the exogenous disturbance processes.
49:1796:134235:18:18:89:539:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A  useful  question  about  these  optimal  responses  is  the  degree  to  which  they  can  be
49:1797:134331:18:17:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:achieved through one or another rule for the conduct of monetary policy.  Given our results
49:1798:134422:17:18:72:540:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  the  special  case  treated  in  the  previous  section,  one  obvious  candidate  for  a  rule  is
49:1799:134526:18:18:72:540:210:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:flexible  inflation  targeting,here  understood  to  mean  a  commitment  to  adjust  the  policy
49:1800:134623:18:19:72:539:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate as necessary to ensure that the target criterion (4.8) holds at all times.64Other simple
49:1801:134716:19:15:81:539:173:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:64More  precisely,  the  target  criterion  that  we  assume  is  the  one  that  characterizes  optimal  policy  in
49:1802:134832:15:12:72:540:158:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the representative-household model.  The target criterion discussed in the previous section corresponded to
49:1803:134939:12:12:72:539:146:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:optimal policy in a representative household modelin which the steady-state level of output is efficient,which
49:1804:135049:12:12:72:539:134:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:required that 1−τ=μp≡θ/(θ−1).More generally, the optimal target criterion for the representative-
49:1805:135146:12:12:72:540:122:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:household model continues to be of the form (4.8), but the definition of the output gapxtand the relative
49:1806:135251:12:12:71:540:110:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:weightλyare slightly different, as explained inBenigno and Woodford(2005). To be precise, in our numerical
49:1807:135357:12:16:71:539:98:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:solutions  under  the  “flexible  inflation  targeting  rule”  (4.8),  we  define  the  variablextas  in  Benigno  and
49:1808:135475:16:0:71:535:82:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Woodford, except that the exogenous level of government purchasesˆGtis replaced byˆGt+̂ ̃Ξt, as in (4.4).
50:1809:135626:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proposals that we shall consider include the simple Taylor rule analyzed in section 2, and
50:1810:135716:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  strict  inflation  targeting  rule,  under  which  monetary  policy  stabilizes  the  inflation  rate
50:1811:135820:18:18:72:323:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regardless of the type of disturbance that occurs.
50:1812:135870:18:18:89:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The equilibrium responses of the endogenous variables to a technology shock (of exactly
50:1813:135957:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  same  kind  previously  considered  in  Figures  3and6)  under  each  of  these  alternative
50:1814:136054:18:18:71:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policies are shown in Figure10.  (The model parameterization is again the one
50:1815:136140:18:18:71:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with a convex intermediation technology, as in Figures5-9.) The solid line (labeled ‘Optimal’)
50:1816:136234:18:18:71:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indicates the equilibrium responses to the increase in productivity under the optimal policy.
50:1817:136327:18:18:71:539:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  dashed  line  (labeled  ‘PiStab’)  instead  indicates  responses  under  a  policy  that  fully
50:1818:136427:18:18:71:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stabilizes  inflation  (i.e.,strict  inflation  targeting);  the  line  marked  with  +  signs  (labeled
50:1819:136531:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:‘Taylor’)  indicates  responses  under  policy  conducted  in  accordance  with  the  Taylor  rule;
50:1820:136630:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the line marked with x’s (labeled ‘FlexTarget’) indicates responses under the flexible
50:1821:136720:18:17:71:200:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation targeting policy.
50:1822:136747:17:18:89:539:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the case of this kind of shock, the aggregate-supply relation (3.12) implies that there
50:1823:136837:18:18:71:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is little inconsistency between inflation stabilization and output-gap stabilization; and as a
50:1824:136931:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consequence strict inflation targeting and flexible inflation targeting are barely distinguish-
50:1825:137026:18:18:71:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:able policies.65They are also both very close to the optimal policy, confirming that in this
50:1826:137118:18:18:71:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:respect the analytical results of the previous section continue to provide a good approxima-
50:1827:137210:18:18:71:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion.   The  Taylor  rule  is  instead  much  less  close  to  an  optimal  policy,  because  it  requires
50:1828:137316:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy to be tightened in response to the output increase, even when this does not represent
50:1829:137408:18:18:71:539:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high output relative to the natural rate (which is increased by the technology shock).  Similar
50:1830:137503:18:18:71:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:results are obtained in the case of exogenous shocks to the disutility of labor, the demand
50:1831:137594:18:18:71:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of borrowers,  or to the path of government debt (none of which are shown here):  in each
50:1832:137683:18:18:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case, there is sufficiently little tension between the requirements of inflation stabilization and
50:1833:137781:18:18:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of output-gap stabilization that flexible inflation targeting and strict inflation targeting are
50:1834:137877:18:18:71:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similar policies, and both are fairly close to optimal policy (while the Taylor rule is much
50:1835:137969:18:17:71:125:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less close).
50:1836:137981:17:18:89:539:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure11shows the corresponding equilibrium responses in the case of a shock to the
50:1837:138064:18:18:71:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wage markupμwt, under the same four alternative policies.  This case is interesting because
50:1838:138155:18:18:71:539:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it  is  one  in  which  strict  inflation  targeting  is  clearly  not  an  optimal  policy,  even  in  the
50:1839:138262:18:18:71:539:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:representative-household model, owing to the substantial “cost-push” effect of such a shock.
50:1840:138354:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(However, even in this case, strict inflation targeting is still more similar to optimal policy
50:1841:138449:18:19:71:539:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than is adherence to the Taylor rule.)  The figure shows that in the case of this kind of shock,
50:1842:138545:19:15:81:539:94:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:65In fact, if we did not allow for endogeneity of the credit spread, as in the model with a linear interme-
50:1843:138652:15:0:72:278:79:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:diation technology, they would not differ at all.
51:1844:138747:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as with other “supply shocks” such as disturbances to the disutility of labor supply or to the
51:1845:138841:18:18:72:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tax rate,flexibleinflation targeting is nonetheless quite a close approximation to optimal
51:1846:138931:18:18:72:105:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy.
51:1847:138938:18:18:89:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 12 shows the corresponding equilibrium responses to a shock to the level of gov-
51:1848:139025:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ernment purchases (of the kind previously assumed in Figures4 and7); and Figure13shows
51:1849:139111:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the responses to a shock to the demand of savers (of the kind previously assumed in Figure
51:1850:139201:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:8).  In the case of a shock to government purchases,  strict inflation targeting is again not
51:1851:139294:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimal,66and in at least some respects the Taylor rule is in this case closer to the optimal
51:1852:139387:18:18:72:539:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy than would be strict inflation targeting.67Nonetheless, once again flexible inflation
51:1853:139479:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:targeting is the closest to optimal policy of the set of simple policy rules considered here,
51:1854:139572:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:though optimal policy would be slightly tighter in the period of the shock.  In the case of a
51:1855:139665:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shock to the demand of savers as well, flexible inflation targeting is the closest to optimal
51:1856:139758:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy,  though  again  optimal  policy  would  be  slightly  tighter  in  the  period  of  the  shock.
51:1857:139861:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Flexible inflation targeting is nonetheless a slightly tighter policy (initially) in response to
51:1858:139957:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the expansionary shock than strict inflation targeting would be, though it is not excessively
51:1859:140050:18:18:72:311:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tight in the way that the simple Taylor rule is.
51:1860:140098:18:18:89:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure14instead considers equilbrium responses to a shock to the demand of borrowers
51:1861:140182:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(again,  the  shock  increases  their  purchases  by  one  percent  for  a  given  marginal  utility  of
51:1862:140286:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:income).  In this case, the way in which the strict inflation targeting policy is suboptimal
51:1863:140378:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is opposite to the case of two “demand shocks” just considered:  under an optimal policy,
51:1864:140467:18:18:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation would be allowed to rise slightly in response to the shock.  But again the flexible
51:1865:140560:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation  targeting  policy  deviates  from  strict  inflation  targeting  in  the  correct  direction,
51:1866:140664:18:18:72:475:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:while both targeting rules are substantially better than the simple Taylor rule.
51:1867:140744:18:18:89:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, Figure15shows the corresponding equilibrium responses in the case of a shock
51:1868:140829:18:18:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the default rate   ̃χt,of a size sufficient to increase the credit spreadωtby four percentage
51:1869:140925:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points  (annualized).   This  kind  of  shock  (not  discussed  in  section  2.3  because  there  is  no
51:1870:141029:18:17:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analogous shock in the models without financial frictions) would be quite contractionary if
51:1871:141120:17:18:72:539:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy were conducted in accordance with an unadjusted Taylor rule.68But as in
51:1872:141207:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the case of a productivity shock (shown in Figure 10) or a shock to the disutility of labor
51:1873:141298:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:supply, either kind of inflation targeting is much closer to optimal policy.  Yet even in this
51:1874:141392:18:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case, flexible inflation targeting is not quite an equivalent policy to strict inflation targeting,
51:1875:141491:18:16:81:539:131:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:66This  would  be  true  even  in  the  representative-household  model,  given  the  existence  of  steady-state
51:1876:141604:16:8:72:327:115:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:distortions, as discussed byBenigno and Woodford(2005).
51:1877:141659:8:12:81:392:107:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:67The response of output is more nearly optimal under the Taylor rule.
51:1878:141729:12:16:81:539:95:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:68This  effect  could  be  substantially  mitigated,  of  course,  by  a  spread-adjusted  Taylor  rule  of  the  kind
51:1879:141847:16:0:72:529:79:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:proposed byTaylor(2008).  SeeC ́urdia and Woodford(2010) for numerical analysis of rules of that kind.
52:1880:141995:0:18:72:249:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and is closer to the optimal policy.
52:1881:142031:18:18:89:539:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, our conclusion is that while the additional distortions that were omitted in the
52:1882:142120:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:special case for which we were able to give an analytical characterization of optimal policy
52:1883:142212:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in section 3.1 are of at least some significance in our calibrated model, the flexible inflation
52:1884:142308:18:18:72:540:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:targeting rule (4.8) continues to provide a fairly good approximation to optimal policy, in
52:1885:142399:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:response to each of the variety of types of exogenous disturbances discussed above.69Since
52:1886:142489:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this is also the rule that characterizes optimal policy in the basic NK model, in at least this
52:1887:142584:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sense the basic NK model remains quite a good guide to policy in the kind of environment that
52:1888:142677:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we consider.  Of course, it is important to remember that the policy prescription provided by
52:1889:142770:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(4.8) is not a complete description of the way in which the policy rate should be adjusted: it is
52:1890:142867:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:still necessary to use amodelof the transmission mechanism to determine what adjustments
52:1891:142955:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the policy rate are needed to ensure that the target criterion is satisfied.  And the model
52:1892:143049:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used for this latter purpose needs to be one that takes account of the credit frictions — in
52:1893:143141:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:particular, that takes account of the variations over time in the size of credit spreads.  But
52:1894:143235:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the target criterion around which monetary policy deliberations are structured may not need
52:1895:143326:18:46:72:384:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be changed in response to the existence of credit frictions.
52:1896:143389:46:29:72:201:372:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5    Conclusions
52:1897:143405:29:18:72:540:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:With  regard  to  the  most  general  question  raised  in  our  introduction  —  implications  for
52:1898:143504:18:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models for policy analysis — our results suggest that the basic view of the way in which
52:1899:143592:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy influences aggregate expenditure and inflation presented in New Keynesian
52:1900:143681:18:18:72:540:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models need not be modified in any fundamental way as a consequence of the observation
52:1901:143767:18:18:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that substantial spreads exist on average between different interest rates in the economy, or
52:1902:143860:18:18:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that these spreads are not always constant over time. We have exhibited a simple extension of
52:1903:143953:18:18:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the basic NK model in which a time-varying positive spread exists between the interest rate
52:1904:144044:18:18:72:540:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:available to savers and the interest rate at which borrowers can borrow.  Yet in at least the
52:1905:144137:18:18:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simplest version of this model, the monetary transmission mechanism is virtually identical to
52:1906:144230:18:18:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that of the basic NK model:  monetary policy can be viewed purely as central-bank control
52:1907:144319:18:18:72:539:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a short-term nominal interest rate (the deposit rateidt), and the ways in which aggregate
52:1908:144411:18:17:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expenditure and inflation are determined by the expected central-bank reaction function for
52:1909:144502:17:18:72:540:128:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the policy rate (e.g.,  a Taylor rule specification) are nearly identical to those in the basic
52:1910:144597:18:18:72:540:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:NK model.  Hence the fundamental lessons implied by that framework for monetary policy
52:1911:144683:18:16:81:539:92:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:69The Appendix includes figures with the equilibrium responses to all the exogenous disturbances consid-
52:1912:144787:16:0:72:270:76:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:ered, under the alternative policies discussed.
53:1913:144880:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analysis  continue  to  apply  (for  example,  the  conclusion  that  central  banks  influence  the
53:1914:144980:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate economy primarily by affecting the expected future path of short-run real rates of
53:1915:145072:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:return, rather than through their control of the current short rate as such, the conclusion
53:1916:145163:18:18:72:343:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that optimal policy is history-dependent, and so on).
53:1917:145216:18:18:89:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This does not mean that financial frictions are irrelevant to output and inflation deter-
53:1918:145305:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mination.  Even in the simplest case of the present model, time-variation in credit spreads
53:1919:145396:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:affects both the “IS relation” between the expected path of the real policy rate and aggregate
53:1920:145490:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expenditure and the “AS relation” between aggregate output and inflation.  However, in the
53:1921:145580:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simplest version of the model, these spreads simply contribute additional additive terms to
53:1922:145671:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these relations,  corresponding to a new form of exogenous disturbance,  in addition to the
53:1923:145762:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real sources of variation in the natural rate of interest and natural rate of output, and the
53:1924:145855:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“cost-push” disturbances allowed for in the basic NK model.  The occurrence of such addi-
53:1925:145944:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional disturbances matters:  successful monetary policy requires appropriate adjustment of
53:1926:146035:17:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the policy rate in response to disturbances, and this requires monitoring them in real time
53:1927:146126:18:18:72:540:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and correctly identifying their character as they occur.  But the effects of “financial shocks”
53:1928:146221:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the simplest version of our model with credit frictions are not fundamentally different than
53:1929:146316:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the effects of a certain linear combination of types of shocks that are already considered in
53:1930:146409:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the standard NK literature, and the appropriate response to them (from the point of view
53:1931:146497:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of stabilization of inflation and/or real activity) is the same as would be appropriate in the
53:1932:146591:18:18:72:295:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case of that combination of familiar shocks.
53:1933:146635:18:18:89:539:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Among  other  things,  allowing  for  credit  spreads  need  not  require  any  reconsideration
53:1934:146730:18:18:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  often-noted  de-emphasis  of  measures  of  the  money  supply  and  sources  of  money
53:1935:146826:18:18:72:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand in standard NK models.70We have shown that it is possible to extend the basic NK
53:1936:146913:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model to incorporate time-varying credit frictions, without making any reference to money or
53:1937:147005:18:18:72:540:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:introducing a transactions role for money.  This can be interpreted as a “cashless” model in
53:1938:147097:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which there actually are no transactions balances and no government liabilities that are held
53:1939:147190:18:17:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other than for their pecuniary returns.  But as usual, the model can also be interpreted as
53:1940:147281:17:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one in which money does supply liquidity services and earns a correspondingly lower return
53:1941:147371:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than government debt, and in which the central bank implements its interest-rate target by
53:1942:147461:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adjusting the supply of money.  It remains the case,  under this latter interpretation,  that
53:1943:147554:18:16:81:540:149:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:70Critics of the omission of a fundamental role for monetary aggregates in NK models (e.g.,Issing, 2006;
53:1944:147658:16:12:72:540:133:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Goodhart,2007) often point to the absence of multiple interest rates and of any role for financial interme-
53:1945:147765:12:12:72:540:121:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:diaries as a ground for suspecting the empirical relevance of such models.  Goodhart, in particular, proposes
53:1946:147874:12:12:72:540:109:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:that the absence of financial frictions in such models may account for the absence of an essential role for
53:1947:147981:12:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:money:   “by  basing  their  model  on  [frictionless  financial  markets],  the  Neo-Keynesians  are  turning  their
53:1948:148098:12:12:72:539:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:model into an essentiallynon-monetarymodel.  So it is no surprise that monetary variables are inessential
53:1949:148203:12:0:71:131:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in it” (p.  11).
54:1950:148265:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what matters about monetary policy is the intended reaction function for interest rates, and
54:1951:148357:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not the adjustments of the supply of money that are required in order to achieve the interest-
54:1952:148451:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate targets,  and that,  under a plausible calibration of the size of monetary frictions,  the
54:1953:148546:18:18:72:540:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:existence of such frictions is of negligible quantitative significance for the predicted evolution
54:1954:148644:18:18:72:256:615:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of aggregate activity and inflation.71
54:1955:148682:18:18:89:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Yet while our results suggest that in the case of many types of aggregate disturbances
54:1956:148768:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(both  disturbances  that  are  ordinarily  thought  of  as  “demand”  disturbances,  and  others
54:1957:148865:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that are considered “supply” disturbances), the effects of shocks on the evolution of output,
54:1958:148958:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation and interest rates under a conventional specification of monetary policy are not too
54:1959:149052:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:greatly changed by the introduction of credit frictions, this is not uniformly the case.  One
54:1960:149145:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:example  is  the  effects  of  changes  in  the  path  of  government  debt  owing  to  shifts  in  fiscal
54:1961:149251:18:18:72:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy.  While the path of government debt hasnoeffects on inflation, output or interest-rate
54:1962:149344:18:17:71:539:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determination in the basic NK model (if distorting tax rates are assumed not to change, so
54:1963:149434:17:18:71:539:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the changed path of government borrowing corresponds only to a change in the time
54:1964:149520:18:18:71:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:path of net lump-sum transfers from the government) — that is,  “Ricardian equivalence”
54:1965:149607:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obtains — in the presence of credit frictions of the kind modeled here, this is no longer the
54:1966:149700:18:18:71:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case (even under the special assumption about tax rates).  This suggests that the integration
54:1967:149793:18:18:71:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of fiscal variables into models used in central banks for monetary policy analysis may deserve
54:1968:149887:18:18:71:267:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a higher place on the research agenda.
54:1969:149925:18:18:89:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another important consequence of allowing for credit spreads, of course, is the possibility
54:1970:150016:18:18:71:539:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of considering how a central bank should respond to observed variation in such spreads.  It is
54:1971:150110:18:18:71:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:often argued that widening credit spreads provide aprima faciecase for the appropriateness of
54:1972:150203:18:18:71:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lowering the central bank’s policy rate.  The argument commonly given is that when spreads
54:1973:150293:18:18:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase, the terms on which it is possible to borrow are tightened, even in the absence of any
54:1974:150388:18:18:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase in the policy rate.  If it was not desired to tighten monetary conditions, it is therefore
54:1975:150487:18:17:71:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessary to lower the policy rate, to the extent required in order to preserve the original cost
54:1976:150584:17:16:81:540:221:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:71Of course, our analysis here does not prove that it isnotof value to model the evolution of a suitably
54:1977:150688:16:12:71:539:205:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:defined  monetary  aggregate.   In  the  model  proposed  byWoodford(2015),  for  example,  the  quantity  of
54:1978:150797:12:12:71:539:193:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:“money-like” liabilities issued by private intermediaries is an important state variable, because the amount
54:1979:150905:12:12:71:539:181:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of funding of this kind determines the amount of assets that such intermediaries will be forced to liquidate
54:1980:151013:12:12:71:539:169:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:in  the  event  that  they  are  unable  to  roll  over  their  short-term  funding,  and  this  in  term  determines  the
54:1981:151135:12:12:71:539:157:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:extent to which asset prices will be depressed in such a crisis.  Such a model allows for a type of financial
54:1982:151244:12:12:71:540:145:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:friction that we abstract from here.  But even in the model ofWoodford(2015), the relevant aggregate is not
54:1983:151351:12:12:71:539:133:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a traditional monetary aggregate, but rather the quantity of privately issued short-term safe instruments,
54:1984:151457:12:12:71:539:121:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:such as repos or asset-backed commercial paper; and the reason it matters is not because of the ability of
54:1985:151563:12:12:71:539:109:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:such assets to substitute for some uses of government-supplied money, as in traditional monetarist theory,
54:1986:151669:12:12:71:539:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:but because of the consequences of the adjustment of theassetside of bank’s balance sheets that may be
54:1987:151771:12:0:71:333:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:required if the demand for such liabilities suddenly changes.
55:1988:151878:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of borrowing.  Authors such asMcCulley and Toloui(2008) suggest a one-for-one reduction
55:1989:151965:18:18:71:429:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the policy rate in response to increases in particular credit spreads.
55:1990:152038:18:18:89:539:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In our model, it is certainly right that the policy rate is not the only interest rate that
55:1991:152129:18:18:71:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matters in assessing the degree to which financial conditions are expansionary.  On the other
55:1992:152222:18:18:71:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hand,  it  is  not  true  (except  in  a  rather  special  limiting  case)  thatonlythe  interest  rate
55:1993:152325:18:18:71:539:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:faced by borrowers matters, either; so a full offset of the observed increase in credit spreads
55:1994:152420:18:18:71:539:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would generally be a larger interest-rate reduction than is optimal.  (A decline in the interest
55:1995:152516:18:18:71:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate received by savers, with no change in the interest rate faced by borrowers, represents
55:1996:152607:18:18:71:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:alooseningof  financial  conditions,  insofar  as  saving  decisions  are  also  interest-elastic  to
55:1997:152708:18:18:71:539:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:some  extent.)   Moreover,  the  justification  of  a  reduction  in  the  policy  rate  in  response  to
55:1998:152813:18:18:71:539:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an increase in credit spreads depends on an expectation that the lower policy rate will be
55:1999:152903:18:18:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:passed through to the interest rates at which intermediaries are willing to lend; if such pass-
55:2000:152998:18:17:71:539:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:through is incomplete,  this would further reduce the extent to which it is optimal for the
55:2001:153089:17:18:71:539:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy rate to adjust in response to a change in credit spreads.  And even in the case of an
55:2002:153181:18:18:71:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exogenous credit spread (so that changes in the policy rate are passed through one-for-one to
55:2003:153274:18:18:71:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lending rates), the optimal adjustment of the policy rate to an increase in the credit spread
55:2004:153367:18:18:71:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is generally less than the full size of the increase in the spread, and the optimal adjustment
55:2005:153461:18:18:71:485:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is smaller the more persistent the increase in the credit spread is expected to be.
55:2006:153544:18:18:89:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Still  less  would  our  model  justify  the  view,  which  sometimes  appears  to  be  assumed
55:2007:153639:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  popular  discussions  of  the  appropriate  response  to  strains  in  credit  markets,  that  the
55:2008:153741:18:18:71:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:persistence of higher-than-average credit spreads means thatinterest rates have not been cut
55:2009:153833:18:18:71:539:310:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:enough.(This is evidently what is assumed when commentators seek to judge whether policy
55:2010:153921:18:18:71:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates have been cut by the right amount by looking at whether spreads remain unusually
55:2011:154007:18:18:71:424:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:large, rather than asking whether borrowing rates are actually high.)
55:2012:154076:18:18:89:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is true that an increase in spreads is a source of deadweight loss in our model, so that
55:2013:154167:18:18:71:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  reduction  of  spreads  to  normal  levels,  if  this  could  be  done  without  changing  anything
55:2014:154269:18:17:71:539:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:else, would be desirable.  But it is not necessarily true that monetary policy can do anything
55:2015:154363:17:18:71:539:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  undo  an  increase  in  credit  spreads  —  this  is  certainly  the  case  in  our  simplest  model,
55:2016:154468:18:18:71:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the credit spread is determined entirely by exogenous factors — and lowering interest
55:2017:154559:18:18:71:539:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates  will  instead  certainly  have  collateral  effects.   Even  if  monetary  policy  can  influence
55:2018:154663:18:18:71:539:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads, it is not obvious that this will be beneficial.  For example, in the case that spreads
55:2019:154758:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are endogenous because they depend on the volume of bank lending, monetary policy can
55:2020:154843:18:18:71:539:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower spreads to the extent that it can lead to a contraction of bank lending; butthatwould
55:2021:154934:18:18:71:540:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:not necessarily increase efficiency, even if a reduction in the spread associated with agiven
55:2022:155027:18:0:71:539:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volume of lending would enhance efficiency (by allowing more lending).  A better principle
56:2023:155163:0:18:72:539:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may well be to use monetary policy to mitigate the distortionscausedby an increase in credit
56:2024:155255:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads, to the extent that this is possible, rather than seeking to use policy to influence the
56:2025:155351:18:18:72:194:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:level of spreads as such.
56:2026:155376:18:18:89:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A policy rule that directs the central bank to adjust its policy rate as necessary to satisfy a
56:2027:155471:18:18:72:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“flexible inflation target” willautomaticallyrequire the central bank to adjust the policy rate
56:2028:155566:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to take account of changes in the severity of financial frictions, without any need to modify
56:2029:155659:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the target criterion that the bank aims to conform with.  In our model of the transmission
56:2030:155749:18:18:72:539:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism, it is the level and expected future path of theaverageinterest rate, rather than
56:2031:155840:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the policy rate, that determines whether the evolution of output and inflation should satisfy
56:2032:155933:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the target criterion.  When the relation between this average rate and the policy rate changes
56:2033:156027:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:owing to a change in the size of interest-rate spreads, the level and expected path of the policy
56:2034:156124:18:18:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate required for conformity with the target criterion will obviously change.  The required
56:2035:156215:18:17:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy rate will similarly change as a result of the effects of changing credit spreads on the
56:2036:156309:17:18:72:410:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“IS relation” and aggregate-supply relation discussed in section 2.
56:2037:156376:18:18:89:539:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When the policy rule is specified in terms of a target criterion, it is not obvious that the
56:2038:156468:18:18:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:target criterion that should be chosen depends much on the importance of credit frictions.  In
56:2039:156562:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a particularly simple case of a model with time-varying credit frictions, we have shown that
56:2040:156654:18:18:72:539:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the optimal target criterion remainsexactly the sameas in the basic NK model:  the central
56:2041:156744:18:18:71:539:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bank should seek to stabilize a weighted average of the inflation rate and the rate of growth
56:2042:156837:18:18:71:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the output gap (or alternatively, to stabilize an output-gap-adjusted price level).  Under
56:2043:156930:18:18:71:539:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more general assumptions, this exact equivalence does not obtain.  Nonetheless, the target
56:2044:157020:18:18:71:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:criterion that would be optimal in the case of the model without credit frictions seems still
56:2045:157113:18:18:71:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to provide a fairly good approximation to optimal policy in the model with credit frictions,
56:2046:157205:18:18:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when these are parameterized to be of an empirically realistic magnitude.  Because of the
56:2047:157294:18:18:71:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advantages  (for  example,  from  the  point  of  view  of  communication)  of  commitment  to  a
56:2048:157391:18:18:71:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple criterion, and because of the degree to which any attempt to refine the rule would
56:2049:157480:18:17:71:539:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depend  on  fine  details  of  the  specification  of  the  financial  frictions,  about  which  there  is
56:2050:157586:17:18:71:539:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to be uncertainty in any event, our results suggest that maintaining a commitment to
56:2051:157677:18:18:71:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the same target criterion as would be optimal in the absence of financial frictions is not a
56:2052:157769:18:18:71:118:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bad idea.
56:2053:157778:18:18:89:539:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This suggests that a central bank shouldnot change its target criterion— what it regards
56:2054:157866:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as acceptable paths of inflation and real activity — at all in times of financial stress,  but
56:2055:157960:18:18:71:540:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instead should take account of those developmentsonlyas a result of the changes that they
56:2056:158049:18:18:71:539:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imply for the links between the policy rate and the evolution of the target variables,  and
56:2057:158140:18:0:71:539:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hence for the path of the policy rate that is required to satisfy the target criterion.  As we
57:2058:158280:0:18:72:540:687:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have shown, this will generally mean lowering the policy rate in response to a disturbance
57:2059:158370:18:18:72:540:669:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  increases  credit  spreads;  but  the  exact  size  of  the  appropriate  response  will  involve
57:2060:158473:18:18:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:balancing  each  of  several  economic  effects  of  the  change  in  the  anticipated  path  of  credit
57:2061:158577:18:18:72:113:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads.
57:2062:158585:18:18:89:539:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The present analysis represents merely a first attempt at exploration of what is obviously
57:2063:158675:18:18:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a very rich terrain.  Among other obvious limitations of the present analysis, we have allowed
57:2064:158769:18:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for only one, very simple form of possible endogeneity of credit spreads.72Further analysis
57:2065:158860:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will be necessary before we can judge how robust the conclusions of the present analysis are
57:2066:158952:18:84:72:495:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to variations in this aspect of our model of the monetary transmission mechanism.
